Central Memorial Week

President Wang's Report on the Week's Political Situation 12

National Assembly Unaffected by the Fifth Plenary Session

The Remaining Forces of Fang Ji Will Surely Be Resolved Soon

Military and Financial Authorities Will Not Be Passive Due to Difficulties

This Is Precisely the Era for Our Hard Work and Dedication

(Nanjing) President Wang's original political report at the Central Party Headquarters' memorial week on the 2nd stated: Regarding the work of this past week, I can report on several matters.

(1) Postponement of the Fifth Plenary Session: The Central Standing Committee resolved last Thursday to postpone the Fifth Plenary Session for one year. The reasons have already been stated in the resolution. According to Article 27 of the General Regulations, the National Congress can be postponed under unavoidable circumstances, but for no more than one year. Now, the unavoidable reasons for the postponement are: First, Commissioners Chen Jitang and Li Zongren telegraphed suggesting a postponement, with reasons attached. Second, the rehabilitation work in the North China war zone and the bandit suppression work are not yet complete. Postponing the congress for one year allows us to redouble our efforts during this year to complete these two important tasks before the congress convenes. Will the postponement of the Fifth Plenary Session cause any obstacles? We know that the Fifth Plenary Session has two purposes. First, many hope that if the Fifth Plenary Session is held, the proposal to convene the National Assembly ahead of schedule can be put forward. The proposal to convene the National Assembly ahead of schedule this year was planned to be put forward at the Provisional Representative Assembly on July 1st. Since the July 1st Provisional Assembly will not be held, and the Fifth Plenary Session in November is also postponed, will the convening of the National Assembly also be affected? The central government has given this issue very careful consideration, so it has also resolved to still follow the decision of the Third Plenary Session of the Twelfth Central Committee last December, to convene the National Assembly in March of the 24th year of the Republic, and that the National Government will start preparations now, such as the election law, the organization law, and the construction of the venue, etc., all of which must be actively carried out. So, although it is not possible to convene ahead of schedule, the decision of the Third Plenary Session is still being implemented as before. It must be understood that convening the National Assembly requires considerable time. If the July 1st Provisional Assembly could be held, then the convening of the National Assembly could hopefully be moved up from March of the 24th year of the Republic to March of the 23rd year of the Republic, giving eight or nine months for preparation from July of this year to March of next year. Since the July Provisional Assembly cannot be held, even if the Fifth Plenary Session in November can be held, there would not be enough time to prepare for convening the National Assembly in March of the 23rd year of the Republic. Therefore, the Central Standing Committee does not simply talk about advancing the date, but still decides to prepare according to the original plan of party rule, with the ultimate goal of cultivating democratic politics. Only in this way can we demand true constitutionalism, not false constitutionalism. Only in this way is political tutelage necessary. Today, we must make twelve times the effort to complete the work that should be done during the period of political tutelage, in order to usher in true constitutionalism. Although the National Assembly cannot be convened ahead of schedule due to time constraints, the convening of the National Assembly will absolutely not be obstructed by this postponement of the Fifth Plenary Session. Second, from the perspective of the Party, the most important thing now is spiritual unity to jointly overcome national difficulties. These eight characters can be said to be the fundamental principle of all work for comrades today. Even if the Fifth Plenary Session is not held, we must continue to do these eight characters. Even if the Fifth Plenary Session is held, we must still base our work on these eight characters. After the September 18th Incident, at the Fourth Plenary Session, we already put forward these eight characters. Up to now, we cannot say that we have not accomplished anything, but we also cannot say that we have accomplished everything. We know that revolutionary comrades are all very enthusiastic. After confirming their understanding of the current situation, their emotional enthusiasm to implement it is extremely urgent. Therefore, when encountering obstacles, they are eager to eliminate them, and differences in opinion often lead to disputes, which are unavoidable. Now, for the sake of national difficulties, we must concentrate our sincerity and unity under the eight characters of "jointly overcoming national difficulties," sacrificing minor opinions for more important issues. Only in this way can we be said to be sincerely united, and only in this way can we be said to be jointly overcoming national difficulties. Even if political opinions cannot be sacrificed and conflicts arise, if they stem from loyalty to the Party and the nation, that is also good. Then we can implement the transfer of political power in accordance with the Party's decisions. It must be understood that for a matter, one must not only have opinions, but also have responsibility. In doing things, one must not only reject, but also have the courage to take responsibility. This is the right way to do politics. In a constitutional country, if Party A is rejected, then Party B must come forward to take responsibility. Within a party, if there are several opinions, it should be the same. If one only rejects and does not take responsibility, it will not work. For the past year, the central government has held this attitude of patience and responsibility. It dares not say that what it has done is without mistakes, but if no one comes forward to take responsibility, it cannot casually abandon the responsibilities it has shouldered. Today, we will continue to do things in this spirit of patience and responsibility, seeking unity within the Party and cooperation from the people, working together. If the Fifth Plenary Session is held this November, it will merely be a review of the progress made since the Fourth Plenary Session in being sincerely united and jointly overcoming national difficulties. If we can intensify our efforts today to complete political tasks such as rehabilitation in the North China war zone and bandit suppression as soon as possible, and if comrades from all sides can set aside personal prejudices and work together for the good of the country, then Party and national affairs will not be obstructed by the postponement of the congress, and holding the congress next year will naturally bring more comfort than holding it this year.

(2) The Issue of Inner Mongolian Autonomy: Recently, Mongolian princes have requested autonomy. The central government is paying close attention to this. Is this request for autonomy a separatist movement or a puppet movement? We dare not say for sure yet and need to investigate further. If it is a separatist or puppet movement, then we have no choice but to resolutely suppress it. On the other hand, if this request is entirely for the sake of autonomy, then we want to say a few words. Autonomy is not only needed by Mongolia, but by the entire China. Autonomy is a common demand of the Chinese people, especially the advocacy of our Party. Comrades of our Party have risked their lives to diligently implement the first important task stipulated in the Founding Program. Forgetting autonomy is not being a follower of the Premier. However, the completion of autonomy cannot be expected to happen suddenly. There are two prerequisites for completing autonomy. The first is to quell rebellions, and the second is to reorganize the army. Without quelling rebellions and reorganizing the army, it is like the situation in Chahar Province during May and June, where a small area was crowded with 200,000 to 300,000 disbanded soldiers. How can there be autonomy? We must never postpone autonomy without reason. We must start immediately when it is possible, and when it is not possible, we must first work hard to eliminate obstacles to make it possible. Mongolia has its own special circumstances, but today we have implemented the principles of equality and freedom in terms of ethnicity, religion, and customs, and we respect each other. In addition, there is one thing to be noted. Many Inner Mongolian compatriots still live as nomads. Nomadism requires extremely vast lands. Today, the most important economic principle in the world is to support more people with less land, but nomadism is the opposite. Therefore, there is a real need to change the production methods of Mongolia. However, Mongolian compatriots may think that since most of the land reclamation is done by Han Chinese, the Mongolian grazing lands will be oppressed. This concern should of course be dispelled. At the same time, although we want Mongolian compatriots to progress from nomadism to agriculture, we will never force them. We will simply provide assistance to proceed. For this matter, the central government has established a special committee to be responsible. In short, we will never postpone the process of autonomy because it is not requested, nor will we perfunctorily deal with it because it is requested. What we are concerned with is whether the obstacles to autonomy have been removed and whether the work of autonomy can begin. This is the case for the interior, and it is the same for Mongolia. Mongolia has a vast territory, and the government is most concerned about the suffering of the majority of the people. The items that should be handled for autonomy have been entrusted to the Ministry of Interior and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission. In essence, true autonomy and separatist or puppet movements are completely different and cannot be confused.

(3) Recent Disturbances in North China: The recent disturbances in North China were caused by Fang Zhenwu and Ji Hongchang. If everyone still remembers the frugal telegram that my brother and Mr. Chiang jointly sent on July 28th, and the urgent telegram sent to Chen Jitang, Li Zongren, and Cha Tingkai on September 6th, you will know that this disturbance was not entirely unexpected. In the frugal telegram, I made a statement that Chahar Province could not possibly support so many disbanded soldiers, and I pointed out that the loss of Duolun the previous time was due to the excessive number of disbanded soldiers stationed there. After they ate and burned everything, they could not gain a foothold, and were occupied by Liu Guitang. If the troops are not reorganized, Chahar Province cannot be stabilized for a day. Seeing this point, we paid close attention to the reorganization of the troops in Chahar Province. The urgent telegram of September 6th detailed the contents of the reorganization. After multiple contacts and consultations with all the armies, those who were to be incorporated were incorporated, and those who were to take office took office. Only Fang Zhenwu and Ji Hongchang had other plans and refused to accept it from beginning to end. Some newspapers even thought that the central government had not settled them, leading them to have nowhere to go, but they did not know that they were wolves with wild ambitions and would not accept settlement. Among their troops, there are still well-known communists such as Zhang Mutao. In the past, when the situation was unclear, some people even defended Fang Ji, saying that they were determined to resist Japan. But now that the facts are before us, they are trying to become Liu Yu and Zhang Bangchang, ultimately causing the recent disturbance, falsely using the name of resisting Japan to secretly carry out treason. It is truly the ugliest thing in the world. Fortunately, the disturbance is not very big. Now the Beiping Military Commission is responsible for handling it. This group of Liu Yu and Zhang Bangchang's seeds will undoubtedly be wiped out.

(4) The Economic Committee Issue: The National Economic Committee was originally chaired by Mr. Chiang Kai-shek as Chairman and Mr. Song Ziwen as Vice Chairman. The preparatory office has been established and has been working for a long time. The cotton and wheat loan is assigned to the Economic Committee for distribution and is specifically designated for production and construction. Mr. Chiang, as Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, firmly resigned from his concurrent position as Chairman of the Economic Committee to show the people of the country his determination not to divert the loan for military use. The central government has now decided to appoint my brother, Mr. Sun Zhesheng, and Mr. Song Ziwen as standing committee members, and they will take office in a few days. As for the use of the loan, it has also been decided to give priority to cotton yarn relief and food relief. My country's cotton yarn industry is on the verge of bankruptcy and needs urgent relief without a moment's delay. As far as food is concerned, a famine year is of course a disaster, but now a bumper year is also a disaster. In the past, my brother reported roughly on the situation of stagnant sales of wheat produced in the interior at the National Government Memorial Week, and later sent the four ministries of Interior, Finance, Railways, and Industry to conduct a joint investigation. The situation of stagnant sales of rice seems to be even more serious. Some people think that the stagnant sales of domestic rice are caused by the loan of American rice. But if American rice is not borrowed, why would domestic rice also have stagnant sales? Then the reason must be elsewhere. This can be seen from this. As for the relief methods, I will report again after a general agreement is reached. Regarding the organization of the Economic Committee, there are many rumors circulating outside, such as how to expand it or add several offices. These rumors are not very accurate. We have only added a Cotton Industry Control Committee because we are currently starting to control the cotton industry, so we have added an agency. Or maybe we will add a Food Committee in the future. It must be understood that we are setting up agencies for the sake of work, and we are definitely not setting up work for the sake of agencies. Saying how to expand it and how to add to it is inaccurate. Speaking of economic issues, I would also like to add a few words about finance. Since the cotton and wheat loan is entirely used for production and construction, what about military and political expenses? Since the September 18th Incident, military and political expenses have been insufficient. This is a fact that everyone knows and does not need to be elaborated on. What is most painful is that there are only maintenance expenses and no project expenses, and even the maintenance expenses are insufficient. If the military and government only aim for maintenance and do not use it for projects, what is the point? There is no need to say much about the indispensability of project expenses. The bandit suppression in Jiangxi can be taken as an example. At present, bandit suppression in Jiangxi requires money for military operations, and even more money is needed to provide relief to the local areas after the bandits are driven away. Because those areas have been completely destroyed by the communists using extremely cruel scorched-earth tactics when they withdrew. They have truly become a land of nothingness. There are no houses, no cattle, no farm tools, and no seeds. How can the remaining people live in this place? After we recover the bandit areas, we often hope that the people can work together to defend themselves to prevent the communists from coming again. However, one needs tools to make a living, and one can only defend oneself if one can make a living. There is no way to obtain the tools of survival, so how can we talk about self-defense? Therefore, after the communists are gone, the bandit suppression work must focus on the economic revival of the countryside. And the urgent task of revival is first to save the dying. Saving the dying first requires enabling them to make a living. All the houses, fields, cattle, farm tools, and seeds that were destroyed by the bandits must be prepared one by one. One can only defend oneself if one can make a living, and only by being able to defend oneself can one prevent the communists from trampling on them again. From this, it can be seen that bandit suppression work is not only about military affairs, but especially about finance. Today, some people only advocate austerity, and even advocate doing nothing and governing, which is really not paying attention to this. However, where does this economic relief come from? The difficulties of military and political expenses are already such, and the urgent need for finance after the recovery of the bandit areas is also such. The difficulties faced by the political and military authorities can be seen from this one aspect. The other day, my brother went to Shanghai to meet with Mr. Song Ziwen to discuss this issue. Although I thought of some solutions, I cannot report them for the time being until the central government makes a decision. In short, today is precisely the era for our comrades to work hard and dedicate ourselves. Because it is hard, we must work hard. Because it is poor, we must especially dedicate ourselves. Everything can be sacrificed, but the responsibility of saving the country cannot be shirked. Everything can be conceded, but the spirit of going to the rescue cannot but be active. The responsibility for saving the country and preserving its existence is inescapable. (Central News Agency telegram on the 2nd)

Ministry of Finance Plans to Issue New Treasury Bonds 14

Totaling Approximately 50 Million Yuan

From January of this year to the present, the government has repaid several tens of millions of yuan in domestic debt principal and interest each month. Although the collateral for these bonds is customs and consolidated taxes, the central government has actually reduced its burden by several tens of millions of yuan. It is planned to use this collateral to continue issuing treasury bonds. To take into account the financial capacity of the banking sector, the offering will be spread over several months. Rural Economic Focus on Investigation – Reality 16

Rural economy in China's economic problems. Has a very important relationship. The whole country, from top to bottom. All are paying close attention. On the government side, it is being discussed alongside the issue of controlled economy. In general society and academic circles. It is also recognized that if this rural problem. If a solution is not properly obtained. Then all economic construction. All cannot establish a foundation. These are all essential arguments. Ancient Confucian scholars discussed politics. Both take the farming and weaving of peasants. As the foundation of regulating the family, governing the country, and pacifying the world. Up until modern times. Capitalist economic organizations. Imported into China. Mechanical industry. Gradually developed. The old economic structure centered on agriculture. Then completely transformed and tended toward cities. Modern economic society. Superficially, it focuses on "exchange". In reality, it still lies in the production organization of large industries. And the economic turnover frequency of industrial production and financial capital. Compared with agricultural production, which turns over only once a year or half a year. Cannot be measured in the same way. Thus, agriculture is increasingly difficult to establish a foothold. What's more, in the past five years. The world economic panic is intensifying. Dumping policies are prevalent. Our Republic of China cannot establish high tariffs for defense. Nor can it mobilize the entire country for economic competition. Then, our rural areas, lacking organizational strength. Have no choice but to be the first to suffer its ruin.

Due to the collapse of the rural economy. On the one hand, it intensifies the general economic panic. On the other hand, it stimulates social unrest. Thus, "Revitalizing the countryside." Has become a common and consistent trend across the country. Rural economic surveys. Have also been implemented in order. In terms of current needs. This matter is truly indispensable and should not be delayed. What a pity is that this kind of investigation. Only belongs to small-scale actions. The number of investigators is only a few or a dozen. The surveyed area. Only three or four provinces. And in the three or four provinces. Only part of it is reached. The information obtained at most only reflects the situation in a certain place. But for solving the entire Chinese rural economic problem. The effect is very small. Therefore, we earnestly hope that the Economic Committee. Can pay close attention to this issue. Conduct a concrete investigation of the whole country on a large scale. Then plan a solution. Then not only will it directly help to properly understand the rural economic organization. Indirectly, it can also assist in promoting political construction. What is most needed in today's rural economic survey. Is the following three points. First, attention should be paid to the turnover of rural finance. My country's rural technology. Is really inferior to others. But the diligence of the farmers. Is rare in the world. Limited only by the season. In the northern provinces. Harvested once a year. Its financial turnover. Therefore, it must also be once a year. The Yangtze River basin is at most twice. Therefore, it must also be turned over every six months. Its inability to adapt to the current general economic situation is obvious. If this status quo is not reformed quickly. Then the countryside will become more and more exhausted. Second. We must begin an investigation of land relations. My country's agricultural villages. Have long formed a system of overly small farms. Regardless of whether they are owner-farmers or tenant farmers. The living standards are extremely low. Land distribution. Each place is the same. And the central government. Also lacks accurate statistics on this. Local governments. Also lack detailed investigations. The preliminary work of revitalizing the countryside in the future. Must be based on the distribution of land. Seek a solid understanding. Then deal with them separately. Only then can disputes be eliminated. Establish a foundation. Third, attention must be paid to the adjustment of agricultural products. Although my country's farmers' thinking. Still yearns for the self-sufficiency of one family. But in fact, it has long embarked on the path of commodity production. Once the grain market stagnates. The economy will lose its balance. The result of rural decline. Reflected in the cities. At this time. We must truly understand the special circumstances of agricultural products in the source areas. Or set up a grain public sale market. Or the national treasury subsidizes the losses of farmers. As a regulator, then the rural economy. Then there is a chance for regeneration.

In short. My country's national economy. Due to the suffocation of the agricultural economy. Causing the entire society to stagnate at the point of death. Suppose. Today, if we can transcend this point. Then economic revival. Can be expected in the coming years. And its only method. Is to see whether the rural problem can be solved as

All Germany Celebrates the Autumn Harvest Festival 17

Hitler Addresses 500,000 Citizens

Sacredness of Labor, Acknowledging Farmers as Pillars of the State

National Socialist Revolution in Preserving the Nation and Developing Democracy

(Berlin) Today Germany is holding a National Harvest Thanksgiving Festival.

The location is at the foot of the Pogberg Mountain in Heimelon. On this day, due to the sunny weather, coupled with the fact that Premier Hitler himself came to give a speech, the number of farmers gathered from all over the country reached 500,000, which is truly an unprecedented grand gathering. (National Telegram on the 1st)

(Berlin) When Premier Hitler arrived at the meeting, 20,000 National Socialist Party soldiers guarded the road. There were also many people accompanying Mr. Hitler. After Agriculture Minister Darré gave a speech, Mr. Hitler took the stage to address the crowd, saying that the National Socialist Party revolution abolished all distinctions of status and class, and allowed both mental and physical work to regain a place of honor in Germany. Therefore, the National Socialist Party revolution is truly great. Mr. Hitler continued, "Liberalism excessively rewarded individual personality, causing individual status to (rise into the clouds, Marxism takes all of humanity as its object, neither of which is as enthusiastic as National Socialism in supporting its own nation. It must be understood that those who cultivate the soil to feed the people and develop families for a long time are the most respectable representatives of the German nation. Farmers are the pillars of Germany and its only guarantee for the future. Our political struggle is purely to preserve our nation and not to conquer foreign nations." Mr. Hitler concluded that all economic losses in Germany can be remedied. For example, if a citizen goes bankrupt, they can still run a business again if absolutely necessary. But if a farmer's cultivated land is taken away, the loss to the national economy can never be recovered. Therefore, we are determined to save German farmers. However, this kind of cause takes a very long time and cannot be accomplished overnight. We once spent eight months stopping Germany's decline, but if we want to save the German people and German farmers, farmers must have faith in us." (Havas Telegram on the 1st)

Roosevelt Goes to Chicago to Attend Veterans' Convention 20

New Monetary Policy May Be Revealed

Relief Plans and Credit Expansion Go Hand in Hand

Hyde Park - U.S. President Roosevelt will depart from here at 5:00 PM tonight for Chicago, where he will address the annual convention of the American Legion tomorrow. This organization is the most influential non-partisan group. According to New York dispatches, the financial circles of that city hope that Roosevelt will announce a new economic policy in his speech. However, regarding the content of the speech, there has been no indication as of tonight. White House staff also declined to comment on Senator Harrison's proposal to directly inflate the currency to pay veterans' pensions. Currently, veterans are being incited by those advocating currency inflation, hoping to overturn the approved reduction in disability pensions and advocating for currency inflation. However, the veterans have not yet expressed their position. Today, many of the President's close advisors advised him not to go to Chicago, saying that the trip might be politically dangerous. The whole country is waiting anxiously for his monetary policy to avoid discussing trivial issues. But by the afternoon, the President declared that he felt it was his duty to meet with the veterans, so he boarded the train at 5:00 PM and set off. Before the President's departure, he received phone calls and telegrams from all sides, urging him to avoid currency inflation in his monetary policy. But until his departure, he refused to express his policy on the matter. However, before his departure, the U.S. President issued several orders to alleviate the suffering of the unemployed and promote the recovery of all industries. He specifically ordered Relief Administrator Hopkins to establish non-profit companies to engage in the purchase and distribution of relief supplies. The purchases will all be daily necessities, to be distributed free of charge to the unemployed. In addition, he sent a letter to Jones, the Director-General of the Reconstruction Finance Corporation, authorizing the implementation of a plan to encourage banks to sell capital bonds to the company, thereby increasing bank capital and achieving the effect of credit expansion. Therefore, it is widely believed that the President is still determined to first expand credit to the extreme before considering direct currency inflation. (National News Agency dispatch, 1st)

Italy Changes Attitude Towards Economic Development of the Danube River 21

Sends Diplomatic Notes to England, France, Germany, and the Little Entente

Advocates Negotiating Preferential Agreements

(Geneva) - The Italian government recently sent diplomatic notes to the governments of the other three signatory countries of the Four-Power Pact and the countries of the Little Entente regarding the economic development of the Danube River basin. This matter has now attracted the deep attention of the League of Nations. It is widely believed that the Italian government has clearly abandoned its previous opposition to special preferential tariffs for the countries of the Danube basin. Although the content of the Italian government's diplomatic note has not yet been made public, it is understood that Italy has suggested negotiating an agreement on preferential tariffs for agricultural products with the countries of the Danube basin. In addition, it has expressed its willingness to conclude a treaty with Austria on similar preferential treatment for industrial products. It is said that the Italian diplomatic note also proposed that the signatories of the Four-Power Pact begin consultations on the one hand, and that the Danube River countries also conduct negotiations simultaneously on the other hand, striving to reach a broad understanding on the principle of mutual agreement. Furthermore, as things stand now, the Little Entente seems to be indifferent to Italy's proposal, and Czech Foreign Minister Beneš even has other plans, so he is obviously unwilling to endorse it. However, there are also signs of convergence between the two groups, and it is expected that a joint meeting will be held soon to discuss the possibility of establishing multilateral treaties. (National Telegram, 1st)

A Page of Anecdotes About the World's Eccentric, Mussolini 22

Treats People Like Children

Shares Hardships with Soldiers

Reuters Italian dispatch from Galesivod - Although Italian Prime Minister Mussolini is awe-inspiring throughout the world, he is full of emotion. This can be seen in trivial matters, and it is no wonder that he wins the hearts of the people. Mussolini once came here to observe army maneuvers. One day, he drove through a small Alpine village in the "war zone" and heard an old man shout, "I must talk to Mussolini!" Mussolini immediately stopped the car, got out, and shook hands with the villagers one by one. Then he listened quietly as the old man described his plight. The old man was over eighty years old. After listening, Mussolini said, "I also know the bitterness of poverty." He then took out a stack of banknotes and placed it in the old man's hand. Just as the old man was about to thank him, Mussolini had already gotten into the car and sped away. One day, Mussolini's car passed through the Bai Liji mountain pass and saw a small squad of artillerymen dragging a 105mm gun, looking very tired. He shouted loudly, "Wait a moment, I will help you!" He jumped out of the car and, under the command of a junior officer, did his best to help the soldiers drag the gun. At that time, the scorching sun was in the sky, and he was sweating profusely, but he didn't care. Whenever Mussolini passed through a village, the villagers would bring the old and the young out to greet him. Mussolini would always get out of the car and mingle with the crowd. One day, an old woman spoke to him. When Mussolini was leaving, she said happily, "Mussolini, I am deeply grateful to you. Now I can die in peace!" Mussolini replied with a smile, "Please don't say that, otherwise I will never forget you!" Mussolini always had a cheerful expression on his face, and when he talked about anecdotes from the European war with his own reserve brigade, he gesticulated and was overjoyed. Whenever Mussolini met an old comrade-in-arms, he would call out their name and salute them. One day, he stopped outside a vineyard and talked to the owner in detail, inquiring about his family affairs and this year's harvest. He also kissed the vineyard owner's children and shook hands with every man and woman working in the field before leaving. Before two teams engaged in simulated combat exercises, Mussolini inspected the equipment of both teams very carefully. During the maneuvers, he would get up with the soldiers at 5:00 AM every morning and rest at 5:00 PM. At 2:00 PM, he would have lunch with General Balstrocci, the Undersecretary of the Army, under a large tree, and his food would be taken from the soldiers' rations.

Hirota Kōki's Diplomatic Strategies Towards China and Russia 24

Focus on North China

Seeking to Realize the Old Dream of the Twenty-One Demands

Obstructing Russian Influence in Manchuria

Planning to Deal with the CER Case with Drastic Measures

(Tokyo) - Since taking office, the new Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota Kōki has been in contact with the army, navy, and financial authorities regarding diplomatic national policy. According to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Foreign Minister Hirota's new policy has been accepted by both the military and financial departments. Hirota is scheduled to enter the palace within days to ask the Emperor for approval, and in mid-month he is scheduled to visit Elder Saionji in Okitsu to explain the content of Hirota's diplomacy and seek the elder's understanding. (China United Press dispatch, 2nd)

(Tokyo) - The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs will adopt a positive policy towards North China. The purpose of the visit to Shanxi by Yano and other members of the Japanese legation in China is to investigate the so-called three major railway plans in North China. When Foreign Minister Katō presented the Twenty-One Demands to the Beijing government in 1915, Hirota was the chief of the first section of the Trade Bureau and drafted a proposal to Foreign Minister Katō to include the Yellow River area in the special interests of Manchuria. Because his demands were even greater than Katō's original proposal, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs did not adopt his proposal to avoid conflict with Britain. Hirota was depressed. Now that he has become Foreign Minister, he wants to try his new diplomacy himself. Hirota has always said that diplomacy towards China should avoid names and take reality. Therefore, how to avoid the name of the Twenty-One Demands and take the reality of the new Twenty-One Demands is a diplomatic tactic that deserves the attention of our countrymen. (North China Daily News Tokyo dispatch, 17th) The complete sealing off of Russian ambitions in the Far East is a major task that the new Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota hopes to accomplish during his tenure. According to the Kokumin Shimbun, a newspaper with extreme nationalist overtones, the new Foreign Minister and the military are in complete agreement on this matter, believing that in order to achieve this great goal, it is necessary to first clear up all of Soviet Russia's businesses in the Far East, starting with the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway to the puppet state. Thereafter, according to the military's opinion, which has been endorsed by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Russia should be granted broad and permanent concessions in the Maritime Provinces, Kamchatka, and the southern part of Sakhalin Island. The newspaper also said that before Hirota took office as Foreign Minister, although he had been the ambassador to Russia, he firmly believed that in order to break the deadlock in the negotiations on the Chinese Eastern Railway, drastic measures must be taken. Now that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has recognized that allowing the current deadlock to drag on will hinder the conclusion of other important matters, which is meaningless, the new Foreign Minister is preparing to warn Soviet Russia, declaring that the current situation will make it necessary for Japan to intervene, at which time the meeting may be terminated and a new method sought to resolve the matter. If necessary, he will not hesitate to resort to force. It is said that the young and middle-aged members of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs all believe that the present is the best time to take decisive measures, and Hirota agrees. According to the newspaper, the first step is to invite the Soviet ambassador to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to explain that Japan is willing to accelerate the Chinese Eastern Railway negotiations for political reasons. The second step is to closely observe the progress of the negotiations. If it is still not satisfactory, then a strong warning will be issued to the Russian government, declaring that the negotiations will be completely broken off. The Japanese now believe that Soviet Russia is focusing on technical aspects and minor details, making it difficult for the negotiations to progress, thereby delaying the resolution, which is a sign of great lack of sincerity on the part of the Russians. If Japan joins the intervention and declares the termination of the negotiations, all previous understandings will be invalidated, then Soviet Russia must bear full responsibility. Even if this move hinders the resolution of other issues between Japan, Russia, and "Manchukuo" and makes the situation more serious, the responsibility should also be borne by Soviet Russia. According to a statement to the press by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, although it is said that the situation has not yet reached such a serious point that Japan needs to intervene, there is still plenty of room for mediation before Japan needs to intervene, all newspapers here believe that this statement is only for the propaganda purposes of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and strongly claim that the Ministry has firmly decided to issue a serious warning to the Soviet ambassador. As for the Soviet Union's previous proposal to conclude a non-aggression treaty, Hirota believes that such a move is still far from being seriously considered. Soviet Russia is eager to establish this treaty because there are several pending cases between Japan, Russia, and "Manchukuo." However, if Japan hastily concludes a non-aggression treaty before all the pending cases have been satisfactorily resolved, it would be extremely foolish, because the Japanese believe that Russia needs a period of respite even more than Japan. Concluding a non-aggression treaty at this time would be more beneficial to Russia. Therefore, it is believed that this matter must be discussed after the Far Eastern situation vis-à-vis Russia has been thoroughly clarified. Its true intention is to allow the Far Eastern situation to be adjusted or resolved in accordance with Japan's political ambitions in the Far East before the non-aggression treaty negotiations can be resumed.

Soviet Russia Rearms and Builds a Naval Port in Vladivostok 25

The Military Deeply Fears That Neglect Will Lead to Future Troubles

Urging Hirota to Adopt a Policy of Coercive Warfare

(Tokyo) - Since Soviet Russia implemented the regulations for entering and exiting the port of Vladivostok on August 24 of this year, foreign ships entering the port must use Russian pilots, which has increased the burden on foreign ships entering and exiting the port. Japan, because of the large number of ships entering and exiting the port, has suffered the greatest losses. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs ordered its consul-general in the area to protest to Russia, but to no avail. It then ordered Ōta, the Japanese ambassador to Russia, to continue to protest, requesting that Japanese ships be exempted from the regulations. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a report from Ōta stating that Russia had refused to accept Japan's proposal. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs also stated that recently Russia has been building fortresses and installing various defensive works in the port, as well as placing submarines. Russia's facilities are aimed at preventing Japan, fearing that military secrets will be leaked, and precautions are very strict. (China United Press dispatch, 2nd)

(Tokyo) - According to Japanese military sources, Russia is increasing its defenses and building semi-permanent military facilities on the border between Russia and the puppet state. Although Japan created the puppet state to maintain peace in the Far East, the strength of the Russian side has increased several times before the construction of the puppet state has been successful. If this continues, there may be no day to restrain Russia. Recently, it has also been heard that the puppet government will adopt a policy of concession regarding the Chinese Eastern Railway to avoid conflict between Japan and Russia, but from Japan's perspective, a war of attrition is detrimental to Japan. Therefore, the Japanese military intends to urge Foreign Minister Hirota to adopt a more resolute policy towards Russia, creating the situation that the Japanese military hopes for. It is said that Araki will personally visit Hirota within days to strongly advocate the military's views. (China United Press dispatch, 2nd)

Japan Reforms Military Equipment 26

Striving for Modernization of Armaments

All Officers and Soldiers to Receive Training

(Tokyo) - After the abolition of four divisions by Army Minister Ugaki at the time of the army's reform, the plan for the second army system reform was re-established in Showa 4 (1929). However, due to the Manchurian Incident, its implementation was postponed. However, in view of the recent international situation and the aforementioned army system reform, a new policy of modernizing military equipment was separately established, seeking to realize it with approximately 100 million yen in material preparation costs for this year and approximately 180 million yen for next year. On the one hand, 9,134,000 yen has been budgeted for this year and 6,247,000 yen for next year as supplementary education expenses, so that officers and soldiers can learn how to use new weapons. Officers will receive supplementary education at infantry schools, cavalry schools, field artillery schools, engineering schools, and motor vehicle schools, etc. Non-commissioned officers and soldiers will be educated by the supplementary education classes of each division. Supplementary education is scheduled to be completed by the end of next year. If the material preparation costs are submitted to the Ministry of Finance for budgetary estimates and are not subject to significant reductions, most of the goals can be achieved. From Showa 10 (1935), various new types of weapons will be deployed to units across the country to realize the modernization of the army. (Rengo Tsushin dispatch, 2nd)

Representatives Express Much Disappointment in Their Speeches

All member states should reflect on this, and the General Assembly should bear more responsibility, etc. Other issues concerning technical and intellectual cooperation and the suppression of opium in our country were discussed in various committees. Monument Erected to Commemorate British Airship Disaster 29

British and French Prime Ministers Meet

Exchange Views on Disarmament

Old Wounds in British Aviation Added to New Regrets

One Airplane Crashes, Three Die

(London) - A monument has been erected between Paris and Beauvais to the victims of the British airship R-101. British Prime Minister MacDonald and French Premier Daladier went to preside over the unveiling ceremony. After the ceremony, Prime Minister MacDonald and Air Minister Londonderry returned to England by plane, arriving at Croydon Aerodrome near London at 4:30 PM. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

(Paris) - "Le Journal" published a message stating that when the unveiling ceremony of the monument to the airship R-101 was held in Beauvais today, the British and French Prime Ministers took the opportunity to meet each other and exchanged views. The scope was naturally broad, but both sides expressed sympathy and their views were very consistent, at least in terms of the general goals that the two countries wanted to achieve politically. Daladier and MacDonald discussed the Disarmament Conference, both of whom were very fortunate that the unity of the two countries on the issue of disarmament had been further consolidated during the talks held in Geneva last week. (Havas, 1st)

(London) - When Prime Minister MacDonald and Air Minister Londonderry were returning to England after attending the unveiling ceremony of the monument to the airship R-101 in France, another British aircraft suddenly crashed in Hawkhurst, Kent, and all three occupants were killed instantly. Old wounds in British aviation had not yet healed, and another tragedy occurred, which is truly unfortunate. The cause of the accident is still unknown, and it is only known that the area where the accident occurred was covered in heavy fog. The three victims were Captain Stirling, the pilot, Gilchrist, the owner of the aircraft, and Mr. Wilson, a photographer for a London newspaper. Wilson was sent to Beauvais to take pictures of the ceremony. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

France Concedes to Germany, Agrees to Drastically Reduce Army 30

Standing Army Reduced from 600,000 to 200,000

Enlistment Period Reduced from Twelve Months to Seven Months

As a Condition for Germany to Accept the Arms Inspection Plan

(Paris) - The famous French political commentator Pentina telegraphed the Paris Echo de Paris this morning from Geneva, stating that France has agreed that after the Germans accept the proposal for a four-year trial period for arms supervision, France will drastically reduce its army. French Prime Minister Daladier and Foreign Minister Boncour have notified British Foreign Secretary Simon that if the Germans accept the proposal, France will reduce its existing 600,000-strong standing army to 200,000 before the end of the trial period. At the same time, the enlistment period for conscripts will also be reduced from twelve months to seven months. Simon has already conveyed this proposal to German Foreign Minister Neurath. However, upon hearing this news, the Little Entente was greatly alarmed and sought to persuade France to reconsider the proposal, as these countries have always regarded France as a security guarantee and feared that the sudden change in France's attitude would endanger the position of the Little Entente. Poland, due to issues such as the Corridor, was even more apprehensive upon hearing the news. As for the change in France's attitude, it was because the United States had accepted the plan to supervise armaments for a short period of time, so it dared to make concessions in order to avoid the failure of the Disarmament Conference. (National News Agency dispatch, 2nd)

U.S. Prepares to Withdraw Troops from Haiti One Year Later 31

Financial Power Still Held by Americans

National News Agency Washington dispatch - The 19-year military occupation of the Republic of Haiti by the United States will be terminated in one year. All 700 Marines stationed in this black republic will be withdrawn by this day next year. However, most of the financial power will still be managed by the Americans until the Haitian public debt held by the Americans is repaid. According to a statement issued by the State Department today, the U.S. Minister to Haiti, Mr. Armour, has signed an agreement with the Haitian Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Regarding the military part, it stipulates: (1) All Marines will be withdrawn within 30 days after October 1, 1934. (2) The Haitian Garde d'Haiti, trained by the U.S. Marines, will be handed over on October 1 to the Haitian generals appointed by the Haitian President. (3) After being requested by Haiti, the United States will send seven military commissioners to train the Haitian Garde d'Haiti and provide advice. (4) The U.S. scientific commissioners will be withdrawn within 30 days after October 1, 1934. Regarding the financial part, it stipulates: (1) The current financial advisor and chief deputy tax collector will be replaced by financial representatives and deputy representatives, whose candidates are assumed to be Americans and are appointed by the Haitian President from those recommended by the U.S. President. (2) These financial representatives will guide customs and tax administration until the approximately 15 million yuan of public debt held by the Americans is repaid. It is estimated that this debt can be repaid by approximately 1944. According to the treaty previously negotiated between the two countries last year, it was subsequently rejected by the Haitian Congress. This agreement is administrative in nature and does not require congressional approval.

However, in the past, state-owned enterprises could only accomplish 20,000 to 30,000 yuan worth of work with 100,000 yuan of funding. Mr. Zhang Jingjiang alone was able to accomplish 300,000 yuan worth of work with 100,000 yuan of funding. The work done by the Construction Committee is to create bowls of rice for the people. Zhang was able to achieve great results with a small amount of funding, which should be known by the government and the whole country. Creating bowls of rice for the people is to enable the people to survive. We seek profit for life, which is to seek a bowl of rice. When there are many people seeking a bowl of rice, conflicts arise in the pursuit of a bowl of rice. It can be said that various events in the world are caused by grabbing bowls of rice, stealing bowls of rice, and smashing bowls of rice. There are very few who truly create bowls of rice for the people. We must be like Mr. Zhang, using a small amount of money to secure bowls of rice for the majority of people. Chief Prosecutors of Various Provinces May Deploy Local Military Police Commanders 60

(Nanjing) The Chief Prosecutors of our country's various provinces cannot deploy the local military police authorities, which often makes it difficult for them to perform their duties. If public security bureaus and other agencies disregard this order, they may be directly punished and their superiors may be asked to investigate and execute the punishment. Measures for Taxing Locally Produced Tobacco Sold in Non-Special Zones 62

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has instructed the tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus of Shandong, Hunan, Guangdong, Shaanxi, Chahar, Gansu, Shanxi, Sichuan, Guizhou, Yunnan, Xinjiang, and Suiyuan to stipulate measures for taxing locally produced tobacco sold in non-special zones. For locally produced tobacco that has paid the special tax and is transported for sale to non-special tax zones, the competent special tax authorities at the place of shipment shall issue a tax payment certificate in accordance with regulations. The tobacco tax should still be verified by the provincial bureaus of the non-special tax zone provinces, and the fee tax should be collected in accordance with the existing regulations. The official seal should be added to the original tax payment certificate and returned to the merchant so that they can verify and receive a tax refund from the original special tax agency. (2nd Special Dispatch)

The Foundation for Zhejiang's Autonomy Has Been Established 75

Household Registration Cleared, Organization Completed

Land Reorganized, Security Strengthened

Various Conditions for Autonomy Proceeding One After Another

Hangzhou Dispatch: In the 17th year of the Republic (1928), Zhejiang Province formulated and promulgated the village and neighborhood system to prepare for autonomy. At the same time, it established a local autonomy training school to cultivate autonomy talent. By the summer of the 18th year (1929), the village and neighborhood organization was completed. Subsequently, the central government successively promulgated the County Organization Law and its implementation rules, the District Autonomy Implementation Law, and the Township Autonomy Implementation Law, and districts were divided according to law. When the 19th year (1930) began, district offices throughout the province were established, and the preparation and guidance of townships, neighborhoods, and lanes were carried out. By the end of the first half of the 21st year (1932), the autonomous organizations of districts, neighborhoods, townships, and towns throughout the province were completed. Statistics for the entire province of one city and 75 counties: Hangzhou City has 13 districts, 58 neighborhoods, 820 lanes, and 6,129 alleys; the 75 counties have a total of 418 districts, 1,223 towns, 11,245 townships, 173,020 lanes, and 864,086 alleys. This year, the first step of organizational preparation has been completed, and a subsequent autonomy implementation plan has been promulgated, emphasizing the county magistrate's personal promotion of group counseling, and the parallel development of political and economic undertakings. The Provincial Autonomy Preparatory Committee has also been established, and members are currently being appointed and are going to various areas to examine and supervise. The autonomous affairs of districts, townships, and towns are legally prescribed in 21 articles. The completed conditions for autonomy within the scope of autonomy are household registration, land, security, and roads. For readers to understand the work of Zhejiang's autonomy, the reporter will describe the process of household registration investigation, land reorganization, security strengthening, and road construction over the years. However, the road construction item has been mentioned in the reporter's manuscript "Zhejiang's Transportation is Becoming Increasingly Developed," so it will not be detailed.

Household Registration Investigation: Zhejiang Province conducted a temporary household registration investigation in the 17th year of the Republic (1928), counting 4,644,815 households with a population of 20,643,701 (including 11,603,889 males and 9,038,812 females). Subsequently, in the second half of the 19th year (1930), the Civil Affairs Department and the Relief Bureau jointly formulated investigation methods in accordance with the Ministry's promulgated Household Registration Investigation and Statistics Reporting Regulations, ordering the districts, villages, neighborhoods, and public security bureaus to handle it. The investigation results show that the province has 4,605,512 households with a population of 21,249,898 (including 12,037,064 males and 9,212,834 females). By the 21st year (1932), the reorganization of townships, towns, lanes, and alleys throughout the province was completed. As one year has passed, the household registration has also changed. In order to simplify procedures and save expenses, the original investigation forms from the 19th year (1930) were reviewed by household. Currently, some of the forms have been found to contain errors and have been sent back for correction. Apart from those that have not been fully checked, the survey number of 49 counties including the provincial capital and Hangzhou County totaled 2,805,391 households with a population of 12,174,202. Regarding house numbers and door plates, apart from Hangzhou and larger cities, most have not been numbered. In October of the 21st year (1932), when the township and neighborhood systems were about to be completed, the Civil Affairs Department formulated a method, ordering that towns be done first, then townships, in stages. It is expected to be completed by the end of October this year. Personal registration has also been ordered to be piloted as preparation for the implementation of the Household Registration Law.

Land Reorganization: Zhejiang Province established a Land Department and a Land Survey Bureau in the 16th year of the Republic (1927) and began to reorganize land, but they were soon abolished. A Land Section was established in the Civil Affairs Department to oversee the matter. Subsequently, due to difficulties in both funding and talent, a two-pronged approach of addressing the root cause and addressing the symptoms was adopted. Addressing the root cause involved formal scientific measurement, while addressing the symptoms involved measurement using simplified methods after landowners reported or investigations were conducted. Now, the report will first cover addressing the root cause and then addressing the symptoms.

Implementing Land Survey: The Land Bureau was established in the 18th year of the Republic (1929) to implement surveying of the province's large triangulation. In October of the same year, a trial land survey was started in Hangzhou. In July of the 19th year (1930), a trial land survey was started in Hangzhou County. In the 20th year of the Republic (1931), the Land Bureau was abolished, and the measurement team organized by the Civil Affairs Department took over. By the 19th year (1930), the large triangulation network extended from the Hangzhou-Jiaxing-Huzhou system to the Hangzhou-Ningbo-Taizhou system, and small triangulation was measured in Hangzhou City and County. All household land in Hangzhou City was surveyed and completed. The ground control surveying and household land surveying in Hangzhou County was partially completed. In the 20th year (1931), the entire large triangulation network of the Hangzhou-Jiaxing-Huzhou system was completed, and one-third of the Hangzhou-Ningbo-Taizhou system was completed. Small triangulation surveys continued to be carried out in Wuxing and Deqing counties. Except for the western land of Wuxing and a small area in the east, all were completed. The original map inspection and household land calculation in Hangzhou City were all completed. The ground control surveying in Hangzhou County, except for the Shangyi District, was all surveyed and the household survey and land survey in the northern area were completed. In the 21st year (1932), the large triangulation chains of the Hangzhou-Ningbo-Taizhou system and the Hangzhou-Jinhua-Quzhou system were completed, and the Jintai system triangulation chain was started. Small triangulation was all completed in Wuxing and Deqing counties, and the work was started in Haining, Jiaxing, Pinghu, Haiyan, Changxing, Yuyao, and other counties. Hangzhou City started issuing photos. The ground control surveying and household survey in Hangzhou County, the right map inspection, were all completed, and the issuance of licenses was partially started. The provincial government also discussed the land reorganization implementation plan and decided that the first phase of land survey in Wuxing, Jiaxing, Pinghu, Haiyan, Haining, Changxing, Yuyao, Xiaoshan, and other places, which should start in the 21st year (1932), had all established land survey offices, and personnel were sent by the Civil Affairs Department to guide the process.

Compiling and Sending Maps and Registers: For addressing the symptoms, the reporting had already started in May of the 18th year (1929) and ended in April of the 19th year (1930), and simplified methods were used for investigation and measurement. Subsequently, as the authorities saw that the arrears in land taxes over the years were very large, for the sake of the province and county finances, they advanced the procedures for investigating land. The field map register was incorporated into the Zhejiang Province Land Reorganization Implementation Plan and promulgated in April of the 21st year (1932). First, a trial run was conducted in the first county of the old Hangzhou Prefecture. Hangzhou County, the first county of the old Hangzhou Prefecture, had been surveyed for many days, so Yuhang was changed. In the 21st year (1932), each started a trial run. In Jiaxing, two villages were investigated and 2,200 mu of land was counted, with 211 mu of unreported land found. In Wuxing, two villages were investigated and 5,372 mu of land was counted, with 2,337 mu of land with unreported tax found. In Yuhang, two villages were investigated and 13,835 mu of land was counted, with 963 mu of land with unreported tax found. In Xiushui, one village was investigated and 4,074 mu of land was counted, with 1,687 mu of land with unreported tax found. Other places, such as Linhai, Qu County, Jiande, etc., also found a lot of land with unreported tax. After provincial personnel conducted on-site inspections and confirmed that there were no errors, they were ordered to continue the process. As of now, a total of 2,336,123 mu in 11 counties, including Yuhang, Jiaxing, Wuxing, Yin County, Shaoxing, Lin'an, Jinhua, Qu County, Jiande, Lishui, Yongjia, etc., have been compiled into draft maps or complete maps and registers. The other counties have started piloting district maps.

Conducting Surveys and Measurements: Qu County is combining investigation and measurement. Within the more than 58,000 mu that has been handled, a total of more than 31,000 mu of land with unreported tax has been measured. Yuhang has already started surveying and measuring two villages. Yongjia, Linhai, Lishui, and other counties are also preparing for surveying and measuring. Delineating the boundaries of administrative regions of various counties is also a land administration matter. After the Ministry of the Interior promulgated the Provincial, City, and County Boundary Survey Regulations in June of the 19th year (1930), the Civil Affairs Department ordered a field survey. As of now, 75 surveys have been completed.

Strengthening Security: Zhejiang's water and land police agencies include the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, the Ningbo Public Security Bureau, the Public Security Bureaus of various counties, and the offshore water police bureau, the inland river water police bureau, and the inland river and offshore water police bureau. In the 21st year (1932), they were reorganized into water police detachments.

Reorganizing the Police: The number of permanent police in the province was 16,061 in the 19th year (1930), 15,056 in the 20th year (1931), and 15,317 in the 21st year (1932). In the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the Civil Affairs Department established a police academy and a police training center. In addition to recruiting new students, incumbent bureau chiefs, inspectors, and police chiefs were selected for training over the years. Furthermore, the Civil Affairs Department supervised the opening of permanent police refresher courses in various areas. After police equipment was confiscated by warlords before the 16th year of the Republic (1927), there was a severe shortage. In the 18th year (1929), Liaoning rifles were purchased, but wooden-holster pistols were still insufficient. In the 21st year (1932), quick-firing rifles were acquired from the central government at cost, and more than 1,400 old rifles were repaired and made usable. Police expenses totaled 3.65 million in the 19th year (1930), 3.83 million in the 20th year (1931), and 3.97 million in the 21st year (1932). The water police have been reorganized in accordance with the police team organization since April this year (1932) and have been redeployed for defense.

Detailed Information on Losses in Each District of Chongming's Second Flood 76

Flooded Area Over 1,300 Square Miles

Over 36,400 Disaster-Stricken People Awaiting Relief

Chongming Dispatch: Chongming suffered a second flood on September 18th, which was more severe than the first. The ring-shaped sheds built by the coastal disaster victims were all washed away. Coupled with continuous rainy days after the flood, the victims were exposed to the elements and had nowhere to live. It was not until five days later, when the tide receded, that they were able to wade through the water to seek relief. Wailing filled the fields, and the starving cried for food. The situation was extremely dire. The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Committee has already shipped grain for emergency relief. However, the civil embankments have been completely destroyed and cannot be repaired. When the tide comes in, it is like the sea, and when the tide goes out, it is like the beach. Next year's spring plowing is worrying, and the people are greatly panicked. The disaster losses in each district are summarized as follows:

First District: The flooded area includes nine townships, including Hongmei, Paiya, Maqiao, Beigao, Boundary Stone, Hongyun, Funong, Tingnan, and Xiaoyuan, totaling about 60 square miles. Seventy percent of the embankment of Hongmei Township was destroyed, and the embankment of Paiya Township was completely lost. Sixty percent of the embankments of Maqiao and Beigao Townships were destroyed. Five official works were damaged. Approximately 36,000 mu of farmland were affected. Approximately 1,000 houses were destroyed. A total of 3,099 disaster-stricken people are awaiting relief. 19 people died.

Second District: The disaster area includes nine townships, including Zhengfeng, Fumin, Yunbei, Yangdong, Yangxi, Yunnan, Zanhua, Yongping, and Bangzhen, totaling approximately 178 square miles. The embankments of Zhengfeng, Fumin, Yangdong, Yangxi, and Yongping Townships and Yongping Sand were completely destroyed. More than nine li of the embankment of Yunbei Township was destroyed. Approximately 11,500 mu of farmland were affected. 697 houses were destroyed. A total of 2,956 disaster-stricken people are awaiting relief.

Third District: The disaster area includes 19 townships and towns, including Shuqiao, Xiangtong, Zhidong, Tadun, Zhixi, Xixie, Xiedong, Xiejia, Dachun, Tianfen, Sanguan, Sanxin, Hezhen, Hongjiqiao, Min'anqiao, Nanxin, and Bali Xinhe, totaling approximately 313 square miles. The coastal embankments of Shuqiao, Chunxiang, Tongzhi, Dongta, Dunxie, Dongxie, Jiaxie, Jimin, Haiqiao, and Nanxin, etc., were all destroyed. Approximately 108,870 mu of farmland were affected. 1,975 houses were destroyed. A total of 7,786 disaster-stricken people are awaiting relief. 27 people died.

Fourth District: The flooded area includes 16 townships and towns, including Yiyou, Hexing, Yonghe, Fumin, Yongsheng, Hezhen, Maqiao, Datongji, Meiyuan, Qiongyu, Huimin, Si'ao, Taoyuan, Shuhe, and Youzhen, totaling approximately 243 square miles. The Futou Dock bank of Fumin was completely destroyed. In addition to the three official works on the Huang bank, the protective bank was completely destroyed. In Yongsheng Township, five large official works were damaged in the Huang bank area. In Yiyou Township, two large official works and two small official works were damaged. In Hexing Township, two large official works on the Touwei were completely destroyed. In addition, a total of 23 bridges in the above four townships were broken. The new and old banks of Youzhen were completely destroyed. Five official works in Taoyuan were damaged. Four official works in Hezhen were completely destroyed. One-third of the banks in Si'ao Township were destroyed. 131,361 mu of farmland were affected. 1,183 houses were destroyed. A total of 2,796 disaster-stricken people are awaiting relief. 9 people died.

Fifth District: The disaster area includes 20 townships and towns, including Fukang, Beixin, Cunjing, Zecao, Yusheng, Fushan, Dayou, Datong, Jiuzhen, Jiu'an, Xianghua, Fengyi, Qixiao, Baxiao, Xielong, Limin, Minzhi, Yeqin, Yongle, and Hegui, totaling approximately 269 square miles. The embankments of five townships and towns, including Fukang, Beixin, Cunjing, Zecao, and Yusheng, were completely destroyed. The embankments of nine townships and towns, including Jiu'an, Xianghua, Fengyi, Qixiao, Baxiao, Xielong, Minzhi, Yeqin, and Yongle, were also more than half destroyed. Approximately 95,400 mu of farmland were affected. 3,861 houses were destroyed. A total of 14,231 disaster-stricken people are awaiting relief. Approximately 200 people died.

Sixth District: The flooded area includes six townships along the coast, including Anxin, Dongxin, Xixin, Gaoqiao, and Minzhi, totaling approximately 81 square miles. The three dikes inside the Yangtze River in Lianyi and other six townships were submerged, and the entire Haihong Township was submerged. The dikes of six townships, including Lianyi, were breached, and the dikes of two townships, including Xihai and Haihong, were damaged. Approximately 10,000 mu of farmland were affected. Approximately 110 houses were destroyed. Approximately 3,000 disaster victims. 3 people died.

Seventh District: The entire first wei of the coastal 14 townships were submerged, more than half of the third wei were submerged, and the entire Dalongsha was submerged, totaling approximately 160 square miles. The coastal embankment is more than 50 li long. The embankment of the first wei was completely destroyed. Approximately 110 large and small official works in the second and third wei were damaged. Approximately 5 million steps of farmland were affected. Approximately 1,200 houses were destroyed. A total of 5,573 disaster-stricken people are awaiting relief. More than 80 people died. (2nd)

The Truth About the Capture of Luyi in Southern Henan by Bandits 77

Bandits Occupied the County Seat for One Day

Fled to Ziziji on the 14th

The capture of Luyi in southern Henan by Huo bandits on September 13 has been reported previously. The following is a detailed account of the capture from a letter from the 52nd Division Special Party Department's Fuxing News Agency:

The bandits of Xiao, Gu, and Huo were severely attacked by the 52nd Division's Peng Brigade and the 13th Cavalry Brigade in Fangji, suffering more than 600 casualties and the death of the bandit leader Gu Dashen. The remnants fled north of Fangji, passing through Shenqiu County and reaching Luyi County. After learning that the county seat was unprepared, they first sneaked a few men into the city. When the bandits arrived near the county seat, they responded from the inside and outside, first disarming all the sentries at the city gate. Most of them then entered the city, rushing straight to the county government. When the bandits arrived at the county government, County Magistrate Xu Xizhi was fast asleep, unaware of the situation. He was pulled up from his sleep and only realized the true situation later. There was nothing he could do. The bandits occupied the county seat for one day and fled to Ziziji on the night of the 14th. They were again surrounded and attacked by the 52nd Division's Peng Brigade and the 2nd Regiment 14th Cavalry Brigade. The bandits fled to the northwest. In this battle, more than 100 hand-held machine guns, pistols, and rifles were seized, more than 700 bandits were killed, and more than 100 horses were captured. More than 1,000 hostages, including the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, the director of the Education Bureau, the director of the Salt Affairs Inspection Bureau, male and female students, and civilians, were rescued and handed over to the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce to take back to Luyi. County Magistrate Xu Xizhi was also released by the bandits in this battle. It was also learned that the original security team of Luyi County had five squadrons. Apart from two squadrons deployed in various districts, there were still three squadrons responsible for the defense of the city. The bandits could have been resisted, but County Magistrate Xu of the county ignored the bandit situation, did not check household registrations, did not send detectives, did not contact various parties, and did not issue the ammunition he received from the Sui Appeasement Headquarters to the security team. As a result, when the bandits approached the city, no shots were fired, no one was injured, and they safely entered the city. The bandits treated County Magistrate Xu with great respect and even gave him a good horse and some travel expenses when they released him in Ziziji. (September 19)

Songjiang

Vice President Niu of the Examination Yuan Arrives in Songjiang 78

Niu Yongjian, Vice President of the Examination Yuan, returned to Ke Township from Beijing at the end of last month. He then went to Sheshan to enjoy the scenery and then went to Jinshanwei. He saw that the local villagers there rely on fishing and salt production for their livelihood, and in order to improve their lives, he gave speeches and vigorously promoted popular education in order to develop the people's intelligence. The locals were very moved. Niu returned to Songjiang yesterday (the 1st), inspected the city on foot, and met with Commissioner Jin Tigan, talking for about two hours. He left and went to the Education Bureau to visit Director Zhu Zhaosheng to discuss education issues. It is heard that he will stay in Songjiang for a few more days, residing in the Yin Family Villa.

Suzhou

###章佩乙's Daughter-in-Law Granted Divorce

Zhang Mengshi, son of Zhang Peiyi of the Kailuan Mining Company, was passionately in love with a woman in Qingdao. His wife, Zhu Ruying, sued him for divorce in the Wuxian District Court. The trial has concluded, and the judgment was pronounced yesterday (the 2nd), granting the divorce. The defendant is required to pay the plaintiff 300 yuan in consolation money and 300 yuan in alimony.

Construction to Rebuild South New Bridge Begins 79

The county government's reconstruction of the South New Bridge outside Jinmen began yesterday (the 2nd). Waterway passage is temporarily cut off. A pontoon bridge has been built for land traffic. The local steamship industry association petitioned the county government to designate a public wharf for ship stops. The county government has designated the Yuanbei Shipping Bureau and the Heping Wharf as public wharves and ordered the Public Security Bureau to send police to oversee.

Wuxi

Rice Shop Bankruptcy Causes Debt Disputes 80

The Jiangyin Qingyang Shen Changyuan Rice Shop, established by the brothers Shen Jinqing, Shen Liangshi, and Shen Jizhi, was a large-scale operation. However, it suddenly went bankrupt the year before last, owing over 200,000 yuan in drafts to local Yongji Run, Ruichang Run, Fuyuan, and other money shops. After the money shops sued the Jiangyin County Government, a judgment was issued on February 26th of this year, ordering the three brothers, Shen Jinqing, etc., to be jointly responsible for repaying the principal and interest of the debt, totaling 200,670 yuan. The shops were planning to request the auction of the fields and properties that had been seized provisionally. Unexpectedly, Shen Jinqing and others appealed to the High Court, which rejected the appeal. It is said that they have appealed to the Supreme Court, hoping to delay the matter and obstruct the creditors. The Shen Changyuan Rice Shop, which has already been sealed, continues to operate as usual, and the rent for the leased fields is still being collected. The money shops believe that the Shens are deliberately trying to evade their debts, which is extremely hateful. Therefore, they sent a letter to the County Chamber of Commerce, requesting it to forward the matter to the Ministry and the Yuan for a swift dismissal to maintain financial stability. After receiving the letter, the County Chamber of Commerce, considering the decline in the commercial market in recent years and the lack of financial flexibility in the market, and that the shop's huge debt has been delayed for too long and the shop even removed the official seals, showing contempt for the law, specially petitioned the Ministry of Judicial Administration and the Supreme Court yesterday, requesting that the shop's appeal be swiftly dismissed and that the Jiangyin County Government be ordered to immediately execute the auction of the fields and properties that have already been provisionally seized.

Water Police Arrest Lake Bandits 81

Zhang Jisheng, captain of the 8th Detachment of the Water Police of the 2nd District of the Waterborne Public Security Force of the Province, stationed in Dongting Dongshan, received a confidential tip the day before yesterday that two bandits, Zhu Gengsheng and Ma Jugeng, who had been robbing ships on Taihu Lake, were hiding in a grass shed in a lake port. He was asked to arrest them. After receiving the report, Captain Zhang immediately dispatched armed water police to the address to make the arrest. Both Zhu and Ma were apprehended and, after questioning, confessed to the robberies. Yesterday, the two criminals were escorted to the 2nd District headquarters in Wuxi and handed over to the county for legal proceedings. Furthermore, the newly appointed director of the 2nd District, Wei Zhanyuan, officially took office in Wuxi yesterday.

Jiangyin

Committee Members Accuse Each Other; Case Dismissed Through Mediation 82

Yao Mingzhi and Zhou Linyun, preparatory members of the Ship Industry Association,

accused Chen Xiping, a member of the County Party Department, of fraud and embezzlement, and Chen Xiping accused Huang Bingying of document-related matters. The High Court designated the Wuhu Court to have jurisdiction over the cases. After the court held several hearings, on July 30th, Huang Bingying went to the County Party Department to retrieve a pledge frame, and Chen Xiping reported him to the county for detention. Huang immediately requested the higher authority to handle the cases together. The High Court approved the request. Yesterday (30th), the court again summoned, and the County Government transported Huang to Wuxi, but Xia Leiping and others came forward to mediate. Huang Bingying and others petitioned the Wuxi Court for dismissal.

Apprentice from Cloth Factory Flees with Cash 83

Zhu Jing, a 19-year-old apprentice from the Hua Cheng Cloth Factory in Gao Alley, East Street, yesterday (the 30th) went to the Yongcheng and Xiesheng money shops, deposited 500 yuan, and at the same time exchanged a one-yuan bill for five-yuan bills five times, and then fled without a trace. The factory immediately reported the case to the detective team for arrest.
