Rooftop Thief Finally Escapes 152

Yesterday, as dawn was breaking, a thief in the French Concession on Avenue Edward VII near the Water and Electricity Street area stole two bags of clothing. He escaped across the rooftops, pursued by the victim's family who shouted for help in the street. After the patrol officers blew their whistles, several Chinese and Western armed officers ascended the roofs and searched for a long time across the rooftops of several residences in Hede Lane, Renmei Lane, and Zhizhong Lane. The residents in the area, mostly still in their dreams, were awakened by the loud footsteps on the roofs, causing much disturbance until dawn. However, the thief managed to escape, it is said.

Mi Jinshan Dies on Boat 154

At 5 PM the day before yesterday, the Taikoo Company's Shanghai-Hankou route ship, the Poyang, arrived from Hankou. The Seaport Quarantine Office of the Ministry of Health discovered that a sick passenger had boarded the ship in Jiangxi but had died during the journey due to severe illness. The body remained in the cabin. The Customs Water Patrol Office was notified and dispatched Detective Gu Wenkui to board the ship and transport the body to the Nanshi Relief Bureau for examination and collection. According to Wei Zhuxian, a friend who accompanied the deceased, the deceased was named Mi Jinshan, aged 28, from Wuxi. He worked at a teahouse on Water and Electricity Street in the French Concession. He had traveled to Jiangxi on business and unexpectedly contracted a disease in a foreign land. Despite medical treatment, he passed away.

Inspection Report of Two Banks 162

The 174th Inspection Report on the Central Bank's Issuance Reserve states: "In accordance with the provisions of Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve for the issuance of convertible notes of this bank. The 174th inspection was conducted at the Issuance Bureau of this bank on September 30, 1933. The results of the inspection are hereby announced as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 60,481,539 silver dollars, including 55,372,569 silver dollar notes and 5,108,970 auxiliary coin notes. The total amount of the convertible note reserve is 60,481,539 silver dollars, including a cash reserve of 49,547,539 silver dollars. This cash reserve includes 45,225,852 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuance vault, 2,550,989 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, and 1,770,698 silver dollars deposited with fellow banks. The guaranteed reserve is equivalent to 10,934,000 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 417,269.40 yuan. The total amount of the customs gold convertible note reserve is 417,269.40 yuan. This reserve includes 7,004.69 taels of standard gold, which is equivalent to 417,269.40 yuan of customs gold at the fixed price of 5957. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guaranteed reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guaranteed reserve is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made." October 2, 1933, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun, Supervisors Xie Mingxun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Jiqin.

The Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank states: "The convertible notes issued by the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank in September 1933 and the reserve have been inspected by supervisors Fu Qilin, He Shaoyin, and Xie Jishen, along with accountant Xu Yongzuo, on October 2. The results of the inspection are listed below: The amount of convertible notes issued is 11,177,900 yuan. The total amount of the reserve is 11,177,900 yuan, including a cash reserve of 7,312,400 yuan, more than 60%, and a guaranteed reserve of 3,865,500 yuan, less than 40%. All are in compliance with the issuance regulations."

Tianfaxiang Lacquered Red House: Tianfaxiang Fur Bureau, a giant in the fur industry, is unparalleled in its annual sales volume, breadth of collection, strict selection procedures, and low retail prices. Its business expansion and internal reforms progress with each year, but the façade remains the same. Due to its fame, many imitators have emerged, making it difficult to distinguish the real from the fake. This often leads to impatient buyers going to the wrong stores, causing misunderstandings. The owner of the bureau regrets this. This autumn, all the façades of the main and branch stores have been painted red. Thus, two red houses suddenly appear on the Henan Road side of the Ball Game Field, reflecting the traffic lights, attracting the attention of passersby. It is anticipated that in the future, customers of the bureau will no longer make the mistake of going to the wrong store.

Publishing World 165

Education and Vocation: After the appointment of Dr. He Qingru as the editor-in-chief of the Education and Vocation monthly magazine, published by the China Vocational Education Society, the content has become more exciting. To increase the opportunity for readers to publish, the society has established submission guidelines and welcomes submissions. The 149th issue was published on October 1st, featuring over ten articles, including educational commentary by He Qingru, the results of a survey on the academic interests of middle school students by Chen Xuanshan and Zheng Wenhan, the interests of agricultural science students by Shen Yougan, and a recent overview of China Vocational School. The magazine sells for 1 jiao 2 fen per issue, and a ten-issue subscription is 1 yuan. It is available at the China Vocational Education Society on Hualong Road, the Life Bookstore, and various university bookstores.

National Games Special Issue: The Health Magazine monthly magazine, edited by Dr. Chu Minyi, has been published for five issues. The content is divided into three major sections: medicine, health, and sports, with abundant and comprehensive coverage. It is a good reading material for families, schools, institutions, and organizations. This magazine has published a "National Games Special Issue" in this year's National Games. The beginning of the issue features beautiful photographs of the various sports fields of the National Games and maps of the National Games and famous scenic spots in the capital. The content includes essays by Chu Minyi, Zhang Zhijiang, Hao Gengsheng, and Song Guobin. All the regulations of the conference are also included. It is a guide for those participating in the National Games. It is scheduled for publication on October 5th, priced at 2 jiao per copy.

Illustrated Explanation of Taijiquan: Cai Junyi, from Ruian, has been studying Taijiquan for many years and has gained a deep understanding of it. He has recently compiled his insights into an illustrated explanation of Taijiquan, the editing method of which is well suited to personal self-study and group teaching. The advantage of this book is that it first explains each movement and then provides a detailed explanation of the actions involved in each movement. This simplifies the complex, making it easy to follow the illustrations. In addition, the connecting movements are repeatedly clarified and connected, indicating the method of transporting qi and refining the spirit to the practitioner. If readers can carefully understand and read without interruption, the benefits to the body and mind will be limitless. The book also includes an article by Mr. Lin Jingping, "The Physiological Research of Taijiquan," which explains the effects of Taijiquan from a physiological perspective, further proving that the functions of Taijiquan cannot be matched by other sports. Mr. Lin is a well-known Western doctor, and his words have their own value. Readers who obtain this book will be like gaining a good teacher. Therefore, it is specially introduced to the Chinese people. The entire book contains approximately 80,000 words, with 100 illustrations, and is finely printed on Daolin paper. The price is one yuan per copy. The general distributor is the Life Bookstore on Avenue Paulun, and the distributors are the Shishi Xinbao and major bookstores.

Modern Cinema Issue 5: Published by the Modern Cinema Society, No. 190 Beijing Road, the only film publication "Modern Cinema," co-edited by Liu Naou, Qu Yunmeng, Huang Tianshi, Huang Jiamo, Zong Weigeng, and Chen Binghong, is the freshest and most exciting periodical monthly. Since its publication, there have been four issues, which have been well received by readers across the country. The 5th issue has been delayed due to the members being pressed by public and private affairs, resulting in readers sending letters and telegrams like snowflakes. The society, in order to strive for excellence, did not want to act hastily and repeatedly revised the manuscript. It has been published yesterday. The content is more exciting than before, and the copperplate illustrations are mostly new contributions, not falling into the usual routine. The text is exquisite, and the comments on film art are unique. Each issue has been increased to forty pages, and the price remains unchanged at 2 jiao. A yearly subscription is 2 yuan, postage included. Sending a letter with postage of 2 jiao will immediately send a copy of the issue.

Miscellaneous News 166

Maddi Organizes Haining Tide-Watching Tour: Mr. Maddi of Maddi Automobile Company of this port sent a large number of invitations yesterday to Chrysler, Desoto and Shunfeng car owners in this port, inviting them to form a team on Sunday, the 8th of this month to watch the tide in Haining, rain or shine. On the morning of that day, the team will gather in Minhang and depart from the opposite bank of the Minhang ferry at 7:30 AM, driving slowly to Haibin, Haiyan to disembark. A small sports meeting will be held first on Haibin. All team members, regardless of age, can participate, as a way to whet the appetites of the team members. The winners will be awarded prizes by the team leader to add to the fun. Then, they will drive to Haining to watch the tide, which is expected to arrive at about 1:30 PM. After watching, they will return along the same route. To prevent the cars of the team members from stalling en route, the company has decided to dispatch a repair vehicle to take care of everything at no charge. In addition, the photographer Zhao Fang will accompany the team and the company plans to give each team member a group photo as a souvenir in the future.

Medical News 167

The X-Ray Department of the Tuberculosis Hospital Relocates: The X-ray examination department of the Tuberculosis Sanatorium in this port was originally located upstairs, which was inconvenient for patients undergoing examinations. Moreover, the original site was narrow and insufficient for providing treatment to poor patients. From today onwards, the X-ray and examination departments will be moved to No. 4 Da'si Road, next door to the original site. The clinic and X-ray examination hours are now from 10 AM to 12 PM and 3 PM to 5 PM daily. The treatment hours are from 4 PM to 5 PM. The clinic is closed on Sunday afternoons.

Taihe Pharmacy's Renzhongbao Sells Well: The Renzhongbao tonic medicine, issued by Taihe Pharmacy on Fourth Horse Road, is the main remedy for treating blood deficiency, weakness, and post-illness recovery. Its efficacy is remarkable and well-known, with sales both domestically and internationally for more than 20 years. As it is now the autumn season for tonics, sales are particularly strong. Wholesale orders from other ports have a large volume of exports every day, and retail sales at the port are endless, with a large shortage of supply. The pharmacy is working day and night to speed up production to meet the demand, it is said.

Weather Report 170

The Xujiahui Observatory issued a weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday: There are clouds over the Yangtze River basin and northern China. The weather is extremely bad in the Tokyo Bay. On the Shandong coast, the breeze is coming from the east to the southeast. South of Mazu Island, it is coming from the east to the northeast. The hurricane has passed south of the Mariana Islands, moving northwest or north-northwest. Its center was within 120 miles of the intersection of 16 degrees north latitude and 144 degrees east longitude at 2 PM. The wind force is unknown. In the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this port was 80.8 degrees, and the lowest was 63.5 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 85.1 degrees, and the lowest was 61.7 degrees.

Fujian National Games Athletes Arrive in Shanghai 172

The first group of 43 athletes from track and field, football, and basketball arrived yesterday.

The second group, including women's basketball and men's and women's volleyball teams, will arrive in Shanghai tomorrow.

Confidence is high in securing the women's basketball championship.

The Fujian Province delegation participating in the National Games, with a first group of 43 athletes, arrived in Shanghai yesterday aboard the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Jinan" steamer. They are staying at the Great Eastern Hotel. The second group will arrive tomorrow aboard the "Hua'an" steamer. They will proceed to Beijing together on the 5th. Last night, we met with the head coach of the delegation, Chen Zhang'e, and others, and recorded their conversation as follows:

The athlete delegation departs in two groups. The first group of 43 people arrived in Shanghai yesterday, including the men's basketball team, football, tennis, track and field, and swimming athletes, as well as head coach Chen Zhang'e, general secretary Deng Shixi, and others. Chief leader Lin Yin'nan will arrive with the second group, which includes the women's basketball players and men's and women's volleyball teams. They will arrive here tomorrow aboard the "Hua'an."

Lin Shaozhou excels in the high hurdles. Among the track and field athletes, Lin Shaozhou is the most promising. Lin was the champion in the high hurdles at the previous National Games. He achieved a time of 16.8 seconds in the Fujian preliminary rounds with ease. He may make even greater progress in the National Games. His javelin throw of 47.45 meters is slightly less certain, as it was achieved with the wind at his back during the preliminary rounds.

Chen Xingyu has potential in long-distance running. Long-distance runner Chen Xingyu also shows promise. His preliminary round results were 2 minutes 12.6 seconds for the 800 meters and 4 minutes 29 seconds for the 1500 meters. If he has no strong competitors, he may improve further. The Shanghai newspaper mistakenly reported his 800-meter time as 2 minutes 3 seconds and his 1500-meter time as 4 minutes 2 seconds. This was due to a telegraphic error. However, Chen is young and strong, and these results are already very good.

Confidence is high in securing the women's basketball championship. According to basketball instructor Yang Xushi, the women's basketball team is certain to win the championship. Representing Jimei, they defeated the Liangjiang team from Xiamen by a score of 17 to 33. The team toured Singapore and other places, winning all 17 games. Center Chen Rongtang and forward Xue Zhengxia are definitely stars. Guard Xu Sufen is the sister of football star Xu Yahui and is also exceptionally strong. Recently, Huang Shuhua from Liangjiang joined the team, making their strength perfect. It is unfortunate that they will face Shanghai in the second week of the National Games, which is somewhat disappointing. The men's team seems to lack experience.

The impact of the Communist bandit menace. Due to the government authorities being busy suppressing the Communists, they have had no time to focus on sports in Fujian. Counties in the bandit areas are obstructed by transportation, so only five counties participated in the provincial preliminary rounds, with Fuzhou and Xiamen as the foundation.

The Quanzhang Association will host a reception. The Quanzhang Association in this port will host a banquet at the Eight Immortals Bridge Youth Association tomorrow afternoon to entertain the team's athletes and news reporters.

National Games Organizing Committee Standing Committee Meeting Resolves Method for Releasing News 173

All news should be sent to the publicity group for release first.

Correcting the manipulation of news about the games by a few.

(Nanjing, 2nd dispatch) The National Games Organizing Committee held a standing committee meeting at the Ministry of Education on the evening of the 2nd. Those in attendance were the standing committee members, general manager Zhang Xinfu, and the heads of various groups and sections, presided over by Chairman Chu Minyi. The key points of their resolutions are as follows: (1) The reception group's hospitality measures were approved. Track and field and ball game referees will stay at the Central Hotel, while martial arts referees will stay at the Veterans' School and New Village. (2) Several honorary directors were added to both the publicity and general affairs groups. (3) The publicity group reported on Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education's concerns regarding a letter stating that news about the games had been prematurely disclosed by a few newspapers, which was unfair and made the publicity group seem useless. The general manager reported that the competition schedule and other news published in various newspapers were copied freely by reporters at the department and were not officially released. The organizing committee will not be responsible for any corrections. It was resolved that, henceforth, all departments and groups should ask Wu Xinzhai to be responsible for contacting airplane photography for the release of news. (5) The next standing committee meeting is scheduled for 7 PM on the afternoon of the 6th.

Hong Kong Faces Immense Financial Difficulties in Attending the National Games 176

Still needs to raise funds for football to make up the difference.

Athlete numbers have been reduced by half.

(Hong Kong dispatch) Since the Hong Kong Amateur Sports Federation began preparing to send a team to the National Games, it organized a fundraising committee. For a time, it was vigorous and impressive. In addition to conducting fundraising separately, the heads of various departments selected athletes for each event. However, for the past half-month, due to the lack of fundraising success, the original dispatch plan has wavered. Furthermore, because Chairman Mo Yingyue has spent little time in Hong Kong and has had little leadership, it is as if the dragons have lost their head. Since the establishment of the committee, Mr. Mo has only attended one meeting. Since then, he has not attended. Most recently, yesterday, Chairman Mo hurriedly returned from the province. It was found that the meeting yesterday discussed four issues: (1) Recruitment of football players; (2) Fundraising; (3) Staff travel expenses; (4) Sending personnel. After about an hour of discussion, it was resolved as follows: It is planned to select Lai Guozhao, Li Guoqi, and He Jiaqiang from the Kowloon Chinese Athletic Association for the football team. As for fundraising, in addition to continuing to solicit donations externally, we will ask the South China Athletic Association to do its best to help. For staff travel expenses, in addition to the team leader, instructors, and male and female managers being paid for by the federation, the federation can also provide a title for others who wish to go, but they must bear their own travel expenses. Regarding the number of representatives to be sent, it was decided to send twelve softball players, eleven male volleyball players, eleven female volleyball players, seven male swimmers, seven female swimmers, four tennis players, and four staff members, totaling 56 people. The federation will advance 2,000 yuan for the thirteen football players to travel on their own, with the expectation that the funds will be reimbursed after they are raised in Shanghai.

Date Determined for the First National Examination 181

October 20th to 25th

Registration from the 15th to the 19th

Emphasis on practical skills, academic subjects graded separately

Limit of 30 athletes from each province and city

The Central Guoshu Institute held a standing committee meeting yesterday. Those in attendance were Zhang Zhijiang, Li Zimao, Guo Xier, Jiang Rongqiao, Zhu Yonghua, Wu Junshan, Zhang Ruitang, Zou Shangwu, Zang Baocheng, Jin Yiming, Yang Gongshan, and Yan Xian, chaired by Zhang Zhijiang, with Jin Yiming as the recorder. Key items on the agenda:

(1) The Hebei Provincial Department of Education inquired about eight items. It was resolved to reply as follows: (1) Candidates must register their age, origin, weight, height, practical skills, and experience at the time of registration. (2) The registration deadline is from October 15th to 6:00 PM on October 19th. (3) The examination period is from October 20th to 25th. (4) Emphasis will be on practical skills, with academic subjects graded separately. (5) Literate individuals will take a written test, while illiterate individuals will take an oral test. (6) Half-price fares have been authorized by the Ministry of Railways. (7) Certificates for train tickets have been sent. (8) The number of candidates from the province is limited to 30. Accompanying persons must provide their own accommodation and meals.

(2) The reception department proposed that 253 people have already registered, and the estimated number of residents exceeds capacity. The meeting decided that the document department should telegraph to all provinces and cities that only 30 people can be admitted according to the regulations. If the quota is exceeded and additional people are sent to Beijing, accommodation will be difficult to provide. The resolution was passed.

(3) The compilation and review department reported: (1) All of the institute's National Examination Regulations have been completely distributed to the Guoshu Institutes and other organizations of various provincial and municipal governments yesterday. (2) All National Examination slogans have been submitted to the Mainland Printing House for pricing and will be printed in about a week.

All began working today at the Central Guoshu Institute's Martial Arts Training Ground.

Notice to Candidates: (1) Whether in the arena or outside, during exercise or rest, candidates must respect the order of the competition and personal morality, and must absolutely obey the orders of the judges. (2) During the conference, all candidates must wear the badge issued by the conference. (3) The number should be attached to the back and front of the chest. When participating in an examination item, the appropriate number for that item must be used. Anyone without a number or whose number is not the correct type will not be allowed to take the examination. (4) If it is not the candidate's own examination time, even if they have a number, they may not enter the examination venue. (5) Candidates may not bring any assistants into the venue. Those who violate this rule will be disqualified from the examination. (6) Candidates must pay attention to the number of times each item of the examination is reported by the announcer. After the third report is completed, they must go to the designated roll call location at the examination venue to wait for the registrar. Those who do not respond after being called three times will lose their right to participate in that item. (7) Candidates from each unit should enter the venue in formation in turn. (8) When spectating, candidates must follow the designated locations specified by the conference in order to maintain order. (9) Matters not detailed in this notice shall be governed by the regulations of the Guoshu Examination Committee.

Registration Information: (1) The registration period is from August 25th to 6:00 PM on October 10th. Each unit must send the registration form by express mail or registered mail to the association within the deadline. Late submissions will not be accepted. The time of receipt will be based on the time of delivery by the Nanjing Post Office. If the deadline for registration is very close and it is not possible to deliver the form by express mail, registration may be done by telegram. However, the telegraph must follow the items stipulated on the official registration form of the association and a registration form must be sent by express mail afterwards. The number of people, names, and items must be consistent with the original telegram, otherwise it will be invalid. The date must be indicated on all incoming and outgoing mail and telegrams from each unit for verification. (2) Registration location: Central Guoshu Institute, First Lane, Xihua Gate, Nanjing. (3) Registration date: From October 17th to 6:00 PM on October 19th. This institute is responsible for hosting from October 17th. (4) Registration location: Second National Examination Examination Committee of the Central Guoshu Institute, First Lane, Xihua Gate, Nanjing. (5) Registration procedures: (A) The list of candidates from each unit must be clearly filled in with ink on the registration form printed by this institute, otherwise it will be considered invalid. (B) At the time of registration, the manager of each unit must bring an official letter and submit a group photo of all members of the team. Once the photo is submitted, the list of candidates may not be changed. (C) Each participating candidate must have a physical examination by a doctor before departure to prove that they are capable of participating. Otherwise, if any illness or injury is found during the examination at registration, they will be deemed unqualified to participate in the examination. (6) Staff members of each unit: Each unit should have one manager who is responsible for all management of the unit and for contacting the association for various matters. Each team may have one instructor. (7) Judges Meeting: The Judges Committee meeting will be held at 8:00 AM on October 19th at the Nanjing Central Guoshu Institute Martial Arts Training Ground. (8) Guidance Meeting: The Managers and Instructors Meeting will be held at 2:00 PM on October 19th at the Nanjing Central Guoshu Institute Martial Arts Training Ground. (9) Meals and Accommodation: The institute will prepare meals and accommodation for the candidates, instructors, and managers of each unit who participate in the National Examination. Other than the candidates, instructors, managers, and those specially invited by the institute, all others will not be hosted. (10) Supplementary Provisions: Matters not detailed in this notice shall be governed by the regulations of the National Examination Preparatory Committee.

YMCA Swimming Pool Open in Winter with Heated Water 187

Registration: From now until the 10th

The Shanghai YMCA in this city, considering that there is no public swimming pool in Shanghai for our countrymen to swim year-round, but the public's interest in swimming is increasing day by day, with a great need for year-round access, and swimming is the only sport recognized by everyone, but to achieve beautiful form and excellent results, long-term practice is essential. The YMCA, recognizing this, has decided to open the swimming pool year-round to facilitate practice for our countrymen. Therefore, they have specially invited enthusiastic promoters of sports, such as Cheng Yize, Hu Yunlai, Chen Qizhao, Shen Siliang, Bi Zibi, Zhu Liancheng, Cheng Houkun, and Feng Zuozhou, to serve as committee members and have held meetings to plan and proceed. It is heard that the hot water pipes have been installed, ensuring that the temperature is suitable for winter swimming. Recently, the number of people registering to join has been very enthusiastic. It is said that it will open after the Double Tenth Festival. The regulations are attached below:

(1) Purpose: To enable those who are already well-trained to improve further, and to allow those who are interested to practice at any time. (2) Period: Tentatively set for seven months (early October to early May). (3) Fees: (A) YMCA members: $12 per person per season, or $2 per month (for convenience, payments can be made in installments of $2 per month). (B) Non-YMCA members: $24 per person per season, or $4 per month (for convenience, payments can be made in installments of $4 per month). (C) Groups: Only groups of 10 or more can be considered as groups. They must be an already organized school or company, with certification from the principal or manager. If they can only come once or twice a week, a reduced fee may be considered. (Note: YMCA members who form separate groups cannot be considered as groups.) (4) Registration: From now until October 10th, contact the YMCA's Sports Department. (5) Time: Open every day except Sunday. (6) Limit: Limited to 200 people. Once 100 people are registered, it will open immediately. (7) Temporary Admission: (A) Members: $0.30 per visit. (B) Non-members: $0.60 per visit. (8) Physical Examination: All applicants, whether temporary or long-term, must undergo a physical examination. (9) Special Coaching: In addition to regular coaching, if needed, advanced classes will be opened, and experts in various swimming styles will be hired to provide guidance. (10) Benefits: Anyone who joins this YMCA and achieves excellent results in this year's open swimming competition, as approved by the committee, may be eligible for a reduced fee to participate.

Results of the Hunan Provincial Games 188

An Incident Occurs Due to Exceeding the Number of Participants

(Changsha Correspondence) The 13th Hunan Provincial Games opened on September 20th. The session was originally scheduled for four days, but due to a major disturbance on the third day, it was suspended for half a day, so the session was extended by one day and closed on the 24th. The results of this session were worse than in previous sessions, and the atmosphere at the venue was also very cold, without the enthusiasm of the past. In total, only 13 units participated in this provincial games, including Changsha City, Changsha County, Shaoyang County, Yueyang County, Lingling County, Hengyang County, Ningxiang County, Yiyang County, Changde County, Taoyuan County, Yuanjiang County, Xiangxiang County, and You County, with a total of more than 520 athletes. Considering that there are 76 counties and cities in the province, only a little over one-sixth participated, which shows the lack of enthusiasm. On the first two days, most of the victories went to Changsha City and County. During the competition at 8 AM on the third day (September 22nd), it was suddenly discovered that Changsha County had five participants in the women's 50-meter race (one extra), and Changsha City had five participants in the men's high jump, long jump, and shot put (one extra in each). Zheng Yangxin, the chief leader of Changde, protested, arguing that it violated the competition rules and requested that they be punished. However, the allocation department of the Games and all personnel sided with them, arousing public anger. As a result, the 11 units from other counties and cities participating in the province all led their athletes out of the venue, and all competitions were suspended. At that time, the Vice President Zhu Jingnong (who is the Director of Education) and the Director of the Preparatory Office Zhang Kailian (who is the Director of Finance) were holding a provincial affairs meeting in the provincial government. Hearing of this uproar, they were extremely anxious and immediately rushed to the venue to convene an emergency meeting, which jointly resolved several matters as follows: (1) The chief leaders of Changsha City and Changsha County, who registered excessive numbers of participants in violation of the competition rules, should be reprimanded. (2) The competition qualifications for the women's 50-meter race in Changsha County and the men's high jump, long jump, and shot put in Changsha City should be revoked, and the vacancies should be filled by promotion in rank. (3) The allocation department of the Games was negligent, causing the dispute, and should be reprimanded. (4) The chief leaders of Changde and other counties, having discovered the aforementioned violations and made a request, left the venue with their teams without waiting for the Games to resolve the issue, disrupting the order of the venue, and should be reprimanded. (5) If any county or city unit does not comply with the above resolutions or does not attend the competition, they will be considered absent, and the Department of Education will impose severe penalties. After the resolutions were announced, Zhang Kailian also sent personnel to mediate in various ways. It was not until 5 PM that a result was achieved, and all parties expressed acceptance and re-entered the venue to hold the sports events. Although the disturbance was quelled, the sports events could not be completed as scheduled, so the Games were extended by one day, and all events were not completed until 7 PM on the 24th, when the closing ceremony was announced. The total expenditure was only 10,000 yuan. The results of each event are recorded below.

Partial Resolution of Slaughter Tax and Tooth Tax Fees in Beijing and Shanghai 200

Slaughter Tax Resolved by the City to Subsidize Provincial Fees

Shanghai City Tooth Tax Has Been Continued by the Province This Year After Negotiation

After Nanjing and Shanghai were established as special cities, it was proposed that the two taxes, the slaughter tax and the tooth tax, which were previously collected by the two counties of Jiangning and Shanghai, be taken over by the cities. However, the Jiangsu Provincial Government argued that the slaughter tax and tooth tax of these two counties were designated as special funds for Jiangsu education. The provincial and municipal governments disputed the issue of jurisdiction for several years. During this period, the Ministry of Education and relevant departments and provincial and municipal governments held repeated meetings and dispatched representatives to negotiate. Finally, due to the relationship between these two taxes and the special funds for Jiangsu education, the Jiangsu Education Fund Management Office began to entrust the Shanghai Municipal Government to collect and remit the slaughter tax in the summer of the 20th year, with a fixed annual tax of 70,000 yuan, which was an increase compared to the Jiangsu package amount. (The Nanjing slaughter tax was also agreed upon by the Beijing Municipal Government and the Education Fund Management Office, with the city collecting and remitting the tax.) Regarding the tooth tax, the Shanghai Municipal Government submitted a request to the Executive Yuan a month ago, ordering the provincial government to transfer the tax to the city for collection. The Executive Yuan ordered the Ministry of Education to review it, and the Ministry of Education, considering that the management of this tax was related to the special funds for Jiangsu education, consulted the Jiangsu Provincial Government for its opinion before further review. Now that the Jiangsu Provincial Government has approved the consultation, it has replied through the Jiangsu Education Fund Management Office that the tooth tax has always been handled by the county government and the Finance Bureau, and the results have been excellent. Last year, the Jiangsu Education Fund Committee decided to solicit merchants for bidding and contracting, and for the past year, it has been handled in accordance with the regulations, and the tax payments have been cleared on a monthly basis. It has already been approved to continue handling this year's tooth tax in accordance with the resolution. It is heard that the provincial government will soon submit a request to the Ministry of Education for review.

Comparison of the Number of Primary School Teachers in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province in the Past 20 Years 202

The Joint Office for the Preparation of Compulsory Education in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province has compared the number of primary school teachers in each county of Jiangsu Province over the past 20 years and compiled statistics. The following is an excerpt of the main points:

(1) The total number of primary school teachers in various counties of Jiangsu Province in the first year was 9,312 people. (Omitted 2-4) In the fifth year, it was 12,787 people (an increase of 3,475 people compared to the first year). In the tenth year, it was 16,075 people (an increase of 6,763 people compared to the first year, an increase of 3,288 people compared to the fifth year). In the fifteenth year, it was 16,236 people (an increase of 7,024 people compared to the first year, an increase of 3,549 people compared to the fifth year, an increase of 261 people compared to the tenth year). In the twentieth year, it was 19,332 people (an increase of 10,020 people compared to the first year, an increase of 6,545 people compared to the fifth year, an increase of 3,257 people compared to the tenth year, an increase of 2,996 people compared to the fifteenth year, an increase of 312 people compared to the 19th year).

(2) From 9,312 people in the first year to 19,332 people in the twentieth year, there was an increase of 10,020 people, which is 2.2 times the original number. The average annual increase was 527 people.

(3) Comparing the number of teachers increased in each year with the previous year, the order of increase is as follows: 1st, 17th year, 2,300 people; 2nd, 4th year, 1,122 people; 3rd, 10th year, 974 people; 4th, 1st year, 961 people; 5th, 3rd year, 933 people; 6th, 14th year, 839 people; 7th, 16th year, 765 people; 8th, 5th year, 740 people; 9th, 8th year, 727 people; 10th, 7th year, 691 people; 11th, 2nd year, 680 people; 12th, 9th year, 670 people; 13th, 12th year, 524 people; 14th, 20th year, 312 people; 15th, 18th year, 236 people; 16th, 6th year, 226 people; 17th, 13th year, a decrease of 171 people; 18th, 9th year, a decrease of 617 people; 19th, 15th year, a decrease of 2,234 people.

(4) Comparing the situation in various counties, the highest in the first year was Wujin with 774 people, and the lowest was Yangzhong with 4 people. In the twentieth year, the highest was Wuxi with 1,436 people, and the lowest was Yangzhong with 32 people.

(5) In the 20 years, the number of teachers in each county fluctuated. Comparing the tenth year with the first year, the number decreased in Wujiang and Yangshan. Comparing the twentieth year with the first year, the number decreased in Shanghai, Taicang, and Baoying.

(6) In the first year, the number of teachers was less than 100 in 32 counties, including Xuhai, Ning, and Yangzhou. In the twentieth year, the number of teachers was less than 100 in only 10 counties, including Yangzhong, Baoying, Siyang, Jiangpu, Donghai, Qiu, Ganyu, Yizheng, Gaoyou, and Jiangning.

(7) The ratio of teachers increased in each county varied greatly. For example, comparing the twentieth year with the first year, the largest increase was in Lishui, increasing from 6 people to 107 people, an increase of 18 times. The smallest increase was in Pi County, from 53 people to 81 people, less than half the original number. It is estimated that the number of teachers in the remaining counties has increased by more than 2 times in 21 counties, including Jurong, Gaochun, Jiangpu, Luhe, Zhenjiang, Danyang, Liyang, Yangzhong, Chuansha, Baoshan, Haimen, Jingjiang, Nantong, Rugao, Taixing, Lianshui, Funing, Yancheng, Xinghua, Taixian, Tongshan, Fengpei, Xiao, Yangshan, Suqian, Donghai, Guanyun, Ganyu, Suining, and Muyang.

Comparative Statistics of Primary School Numbers in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province Over the Past Twenty Years 203

The Joint Office for the Preparation of Compulsory Education in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province has compiled statistics comparing the number of primary schools in each county over the past twenty years. Excerpts of the key points are as follows:

(1) In the first year, the total number of primary schools in various counties of Jiangsu was 4,716. In the fifth year, there were 6,157 schools (an increase of 1,441 schools compared to the first year). In the tenth year, there were 7,401 schools (an increase of 2,685 schools compared to the first year, and an increase of 1,244 schools compared to the fifth year). In the fifteenth year, there were 6,862 schools (an increase of 2,146 schools compared to the first year, an increase of 705 schools compared to the fifth year, and a decrease of 539 schools compared to the tenth year). In the twentieth year, there were 8,360 schools (an increase of 3,644 schools compared to the first year, an increase of 2,203 schools compared to the fifth year, an increase of 959 schools compared to the tenth year, an increase of 1,498 schools compared to the fifteenth year, and an increase of 48 schools compared to the previous year).

(2) From 4,716 schools in the first year to 8,360 schools in the twentieth year, there was a total increase of 3,644 schools, which is 1.77 times the original number. On average, there was an increase of 351 schools per year.

(3) Comparing the increase in schools in each year, the largest increase was in the seventeenth year, with 1,122 schools. The smallest increase was in the sixth year, with only 6 schools more than the fifth year. The difference between the highest and lowest increases is 1,116 schools.

(4) The total number of schools increased in most years, but decreased in the fifteenth year compared to the fourteenth year, with a reduction of 1,211 schools. The number of schools reduced in this year exceeded the number of schools increased in any other year. The number of schools reduced in the fifteenth year accounted for one-third of the total increase in schools over the past twenty years.

(5) The number of schools increased in each year did not increase steadily or decrease consistently. There were significant fluctuations. The years are listed below in descending order of the increase compared to the previous year: 1,122 schools in the seventeenth year; 466 schools in the fourth year; 409 schools in the third year; 380 schools in the first year; 345 schools in the tenth year; 322 schools in the fifth year; 306 schools in the seventh year; 304 schools in the eighth year; 283 schools in the ninth year; 243 schools in the twelfth year; 202 schools in the eighteenth year; 168 schools in the twelfth year; 115 schools in the thirteenth year; 98 schools in the sixteenth year; 48 schools in the twentieth year; 28 schools in the nineteenth year; 9 schools in the fourteenth year; 6 schools in the sixth year; a decrease of 1,211 schools in the fifteenth year.

(6) Observing the number of schools increased in each year, it can be seen that the progress in the seventh, eighth, ninth, tenth and eleventh years was the most consistent. There was a sudden increase in the third, fourth, and seventh years, and a sudden decrease in the sixth and fifth years. After the nineteenth year, the increase in the number of schools was extremely small, less than one-tenth of that in the seventh, eighth, and ninth years. Therefore, the development of the number of schools over the past twenty years has formed an arc shape.

(7) Although the total number of schools increased in the twenty years, except for the fifteenth year, there were also increases and decreases in the number of schools in individual counties. Compared to the first year, there were decreases in the fifth year in the following nine counties: Jiangning, Jintan, Liyang, Jinshan, Taicang, Wujiang, Wujin, Yixing, and Huaiyin. Compared to the fifth year, there were decreases in the tenth year in the following nine counties: Gaochun, Songjiang, Fengxian, Jinshan, Wu Feng, Pei, Pi, Dangshan. Compared to the tenth year, there were decreases in the fifteenth year in the following twenty-seven counties: Jiangning, Gaochun, Zhenjiang, Liyang, Shanghai, Songjiang, Fengxian, Baoshan, Chongming, Haimen, Wu, Changshu, Kunshan, Wujiang, Wuxi, Jingjiang, Jiangdu, Dongtai, Tongshan, Feng, Pei, Xiao, Pi, Donghai, Guanyun, Muyang, and Ganyu. Compared to the fifteenth year, there were decreases in the twentieth year in the following eight counties: Jiading, Chongming, Nantong, Taixing, Jiangdu, Gaoyou, Baoying, and Tongshan. Furthermore, compared to the first year, there were decreases in the twentieth year in the following five counties: Jiangning, Fengxian, Wujiang, Shanghai, and Baoying.

(8) In the twentieth year, there were no counties where the number of schools neither increased nor decreased. Compared to the nineteenth year, the smallest decrease was in Yangzhong and other counties, with a decrease of one school. The largest decrease was in Jiangning, Liyang, and Shanghai.

(9) In the first year, the following seventeen counties had more than 100 schools: Jiangning, Liyang, Shanghai, Songjiang, Nanhui, Qingpu, Chongming, Haimen, Wuxian, Changshu, Wujiang, Wujin, Wuxi, Yixing, Jiangyin, Nantong, and Rugao. In the twentieth year, the following four counties had more than 300 schools: Wujin, Wuxi, Jiangyin, and Nantong. The following six counties had more than 200 schools: Haimen, Wu, Changshu, Yixing, Rugao, and Nanhui. The remaining counties with more than 100 schools were: Jurong, Zhenjiang, Danyang, Liyang, Songjiang, Qingpu, Taicang, Jiading, Chongming, Kunshan, Wujiang, Taixing, Huaiyin, Huaian, Lianshui, Funing, Dongtai, Taixian, Tongshan, Fengpei, Dangshan, Suqian, Suining, and Qidong. Conversely, twenty-four counties had less than 100 schools (there were a total of forty-three counties with less than 100 schools in the first year).

(10) In the twentieth year, the county with the highest number of schools was Wujin with 380 schools. The county with the lowest number of schools was Yangzhong with 2 schools, followed by Ganyu with 5 schools. The difference between the highest and lowest number of schools was 378 schools, which is 190 times the lowest number.

(11) The proportion of schools increased in each county varied greatly. For example, comparing the first year to the twentieth year, the largest increase was in Lishui, from 3 schools to 178 schools, which is an increase of 18 times. The smallest increase was in Jinshan, from 86 schools to 89 schools. The following twenty-six counties had an increase of more than twice the original number: Jurong, Gaochun, Jiangpu, Liuhe, Zhenjiang, Danyang, Jiangyin, Nantong, Rugao, Taixing, Jingjiang, Lianshui, Yancheng, Funing, Xinghua, Taixian, Tongshan, Fengsu, Dangshan, Suqian, Suining, Donghai, Guanyun, Muyang, and Ganyu.

Special Report

National Martial Arts Competition and National Examination – Yi Ming 214

In the 22nd year, the National Martial Arts Team participated in the sports competition, breaking a new record that has never been seen before. From the county games to the district games, from the district games to the provincial games, they are about to participate in the National Games. If according to the regulations of amateur sports, the athletes are purely students as the main body, teachers should not participate in it. This season, the Central Guoshu Museum is scheduled to hold the National Martial Arts Examination on October 20. According to Article 3 of the Provisional Regulations for the National Martial Arts Examination, the National Examination must be selected by the provinces and cities, and only those who are guaranteed by the provincial and municipal governments can participate. The provincial and municipal examinations must be guaranteed by the county government, and the county examinations must be guaranteed by the district village chief. This is because the situations in each province are different. Some provinces have not established a provincial Guoshu Museum, and some have been established during the suspension period. The county government has not been ordered to hold a county examination. The national martial arts institutions in each county may have branches, or research societies, and they will select national examination players, and the sports personnel organized by the county may think that the sports meeting and the martial arts examination are the same thing at the same time, so the martial arts experts or teachers who have been guaranteed by various halls to be pre-selected for the national examination are included in the sports competition. The county does not distinguish between competition and examination as two separate things, and each district therefore, and the province also therefore continues to do so, and will implement participation in the National Games.

From the perspective of the Central Guoshu Museum, since the promotion, it has been holding examinations with all its strength, which is not only limited to students in various counties, but also talents left behind in rural areas can also be guaranteed. Therefore, letters and telegrams are sent to various provinces to urge them to register. The provincial party did not hold the provincial examination, which means that the provincial party gave up the right to examination. The districts and counties did not receive a clear order from the provincial party, and they wanted to go to the examination but could not, so they had to graft wood and replace plums, and use the national examination as a competition, and regard it as the same. Therefore, there is no distinction between軒輊, in the provinces without provincial museums, the measures are not well done, and compared with other provinces and cities that have national examinations, they are inferior. From the perspective of the martial arts staff themselves, since they have participated in the National Games, and also participated in the National Martial Arts Examination, the distance is only a few days, and the competition needs to be held many times. For the sake of cherishing their energy, before the National Games and the National Martial Arts Examination are held, I deeply hope that the persons in charge will check whether there is such an error and quickly improve it. Do not regard one and two as two and one.

Page 17

Spring and Autumn

Anti 215

— 19

In the past, the word "anti" was a taboo in the era of monarchs, and should be avoided from afar. Sun Yingyan created the "fanqie" at the end of the Han Dynasty. By the Tang Dynasty, because the word "anti" was very conspicuous, "anti" was avoided and "fan" was used. This is a very obvious example. It is said that during the Qing Dynasty, a certain official supervised education in a certain province and issued a intercepted title "Wang Su Chu Ling Anti"! Public opinion was in an uproar, and the exam was almost罢. The censor reported the matter, and the official was dismissed and never reused. It is said that the reason why the official made such a mess was because he did not believe in fox fairies, so the fox fairies asked him to eat a big loss of the word "anti". Originally, in the past imperial examination era, there were many words that should be avoided in ink scrolls, such as "kill", "rebel", "steal", etc.; and "anti" was one of them. For example, if you say "rectify chaos", the meaning is very grand, so you have to change "anti" to "return". This is because the word "anti" is disliked by the monarch, and subjects and gentry people cannot but be cautious. As for "chaos", although it is also conspicuous, it is probably because Zhu Xi, who had eaten cold pork, interpreted it as "also governance"; so "suppress chaos" can still be written as "suppress chaos", and does not need to be changed to "suppress governance". Descending to the Republic of China, this kind of profound rule is naturally on the list of abolitions, so words such as "anti-righteousness" and "anti-communist" are often seen or heard in newspapers and mouths. However, the individual word "anti" has not yet been officially used, so it is replaced by "endangering the country." This is a kind of roundabout way. Although four more words are written, it seems more冠冕than just writing the single word "anti". The writing skills of today's people are really admirable. There are also words such as "anti-imperialism" and "anti-war", because they cannot follow the example of "suppressing chaos and returning to righteousness" and avoid "anti" and use "return"; so they have to be left as they are. Fortunately, the so-called "anti-imperialism" and "anti-war" are just talking and writing, and are所时尚. In fact, "anti" its name but not "anti" its reality, you can大“anti”而特“anti”, so what忌讳there is!

Please think about it, readers, if we were born in the era of monarchs, to create such fashionable nouns and make a splash; may I ask, what word can the word "anti" be replaced with? Is it good to use "return"? From this point alone, it can be seen that we were born today, we cannot but say that we are "very blessed".

Officialdom and Wealth 216

— Zhang Yiping

Whenever I return to my hometown, the neighbors always ask me endlessly: "When will you become an official and get rich, young master?" Although I'm used to hearing these kinds of questions, and the dreadfulness of their meaning seems to have faded, I still feel a sting every time I'm hit by these vulgar queries. After the sting, I often can't answer a single word, just giving a silly smile; because I know their motives for asking are entirely well-intentioned. On one hand, it's undoubtedly like those pointless social pleasantries such as "Nice weather" and "Have you eaten?", but on the other hand, it also contains a sincere concern for my recent situation away from home. Of course, I should be grateful for their kindness. However, on the other hand, the question of "becoming an official and getting rich" perfectly demonstrates the outdated traditional thinking of the old Chinese society. In the past, parents all hoped their sons would study the Four Books and Five Classics, pass the imperial examinations, and become officials, so a person was only in contact with the "official" flavor from birth to death. For example, in the Jiangnan area, boys' nicknames always include "× official;" even children from families so poor that they didn't even have enough to eat and never had the opportunity to study, let alone take the imperial examinations and become "officials," still had good "official" names. It's truly an incomprehensible joke; and the jokes don't stop there. In the past, people hoped their sons would become "officials," so they also hoped their sons would "return home in glory," saying it would "bring honor to the family." Even the neighbors hoped someone else's son would become the top scholar and prime minister, saying it would "bring honor to the hometown." From this point, it's clear how important the concept of hometown is to the Chinese. In unofficial histories and folk tales, it's always the same "distressed young master who becomes the top scholar" and is praised for his "glorious return home."

Besides becoming an "official," getting "rich" is also something everyone enjoys. On the first day of the Lunar New Year, the first thing said while clasping hands to others is "Congratulations on getting rich." Everywhere you look, you see temples of the God of Wealth, and on the fourth day of the first lunar month, many pious men and women go to worship sincerely. Thus, it's evident that the Chinese hope to get "rich" no less than they hope to become "officials." And the Chinese have a kind of "maxim" that becoming an "official" allows you to get "rich."

The Chinese worship "officials" and "wealth" too much, devoting themselves wholeheartedly until death. I hope this traditional thinking will change for the better!

Looking back, you served under the Premier's command, once dedicating yourself to eliminating bandits in the eastern suburbs.

Talking About the Abacus 218

— Master of Qifeng Tower

"Coming without a hair's breadth of error, two 'qián' and five 'kūn' make a family, for a time, it's beaten into a chaotic mess, only settling by Qingming," these are the words of a predecessor praising the abacus. In these years of surging new trends, all things are moving towards renewal, abolishing old systems, it's unimaginable that a mere abacus can stand firm like a pillar in a rapid current! The abacus can well be proud of itself!

I work in the accounting department of a store, and I feel that "I cannot be without this gentleman for a single day" when it comes to the abacus. Although written calculation is also very popular now, most merchants still use the abacus when buying and selling goods, because written calculation is never as fast and convenient. Therefore, even foreign-owned companies and trading houses cannot do without it. When using the abacus, unlike written calculation, there is no decimal point to separate the zero numbers from the whole numbers, it all depends on remembering the position before moving the beads. Ordinary people rarely study this when calculating simple "multiplication" or "division," but for multi-digit "multiplication" or "division," if you don't remember the "positioning formula" before calculating, it's easy to make mistakes! Abacuses are usually made with seven beads per rod, two on top and five on the bottom. In the past, Shou Xiaotianjun of Kuaiji invented an abacus where each rod still had seven beads, but with three on top and four on the bottom, calling it the Shou-style abacus, but it didn't become popular later, so the market still uses the old style.

There are many metaphors using the abacus, such as: for people who are dull and inactive, people curse them like the abacus beads that move back and forth. If you only think about your own wishes, planning for unattainable gains, people call it a "wishful abacus." As for its games, there are several types, such as: playing abacus chess, "Five Tigers Descending to Western Sichuan," "Lion Rolling an Embroidered Ball," etc. The funniest thing is that the abacus also contains superstitious ideas. Please look around, there are never pairs of beads in a row, because the abacus is mostly used by merchants, and merchants work hard all year round, nothing more than to seize opportunities and strive for profit, with small gains as the main goal. Merchants use the four words "profit, loss, income, and expenses" to count each bead on the abacus rod, until the last one, which must be either "profit" or "income." Whether it's an abacus with nine, eleven, thirteen, or fifteen rods, it's all like this, which can already infer a glimpse of their psychology.

Miss Wang 219

— Donghaibochen

Mr. Zhao Ziming has introduced "Master Wang" and "Fifth Madam" before, and I will introduce "Miss Wang" without fear of being ridiculed for imitation.

Speaking of which, although Miss Wang was not born into a noble family, because she has no older siblings and no younger brothers or sisters, Mr. and Mrs. Wang treated her like a treasure, protecting her with utmost care.

Her face is truly lovely; her skin is so delicate it could be broken with a puff, with smiling dimples, not to mention her "passionate" actions. Some devotees of love ideologies chase her like "mosquitoes seeing blood." Needless to say, Miss Wang doesn't need to buy her own decorations, several friends naturally compete to win her favor. She embraces the "open door" principle, adhering to the motto "since they've come, let them stay," and she has as many as six dozen lovers, which is quite amazing, considering her skillful tactics. It is said that she lost her virginity long ago because of this.

She likes to be active in social gatherings, and although she cannot write or make speeches, she is called the belle of society just for her face, which shows how much society values her.

At the age of nineteen, she was loved by a retired general and became his kept woman. In less than a year, she had a child, and her life was extremely happy. But she had other ideas and divorced the retired general. As a result, partly because of her reputation, she reluctantly took out 100,000 yuan in alimony, and now she is much freer.

Miss Wang's life can be said to have come to an end here.

Interesting Scientific Facts

Future Prisons – Hospitals 221

Dr. Reinauer of the United States studied the relationship between the endocrine glands and criminal behavior among inmates at California prisons. His examinations revealed that the endocrine glands of most criminals were abnormal. These hundreds of patients with glandular diseases could be divided into three groups based on the differences in their glandular functions: thyroid gland disorders, pituitary gland disorders, and gonad disorders (the thyroid gland is in the throat, the pituitary gland is in the brain, and the gonads are the testicles and ovaries). The first type is mostly nervous, emotionally impulsive, and mentally unstable. More than 70 percent of them have committed acts of violence, i.e., crimes involving harming or killing people, assassinations, and murder for money. Among them, five were the most stubborn and difficult to deal with, often launching savage attacks on fellow inmates. Therefore, doctors were asked to diagnose and treat them. After surgery on the diseased thyroid glands, their conditions and behaviors significantly improved. The second type is mostly kind and affable people, but lacking a sense of responsibility and ambition. More than 80 percent of them were punished for crimes such as fraud, impersonation, embezzlement, or misappropriation of public funds and theft, but it is worth noting that none of them committed violent crimes. After treatment with endocrine hormones, their personalities greatly improved despite a lack of educational influence. Their attitudes towards people and things gradually became more serious, and they began to understand their responsibilities to society and humanity. The third type is mostly cautious, quiet, and law-abiding people who can usually control their emotions and desires, but sometimes they will burst out uncontrollably and spontaneously. The crimes they commit are mostly unexpected offenses against public morals. After treatment with endocrine hormones, their physical and mental states significantly improved. According to Dr. Reinauer's opinion, a person's crime is partly due to the inducement of other economic conditions, but the most important factor is the abnormality of mental function, which is related to the physical condition, specifically, the biochemical action of metabolism, which is entirely under the main influence of the endocrine glands. Therefore, he firmly believes that ordinary criminals with abnormal behavior can be completely transformed into normal people through the equalization of glandular secretions. Although research in this area is not yet conclusive, its partial truth is undeniable, so it has attracted great attention from legal scholars around the world. Perhaps one day human laws will undergo a fundamental transformation, and all inhumane criminal punishments such as beheading, hanging, and shooting will be abolished. Criminals will not need to go to prison, but only to hospitals; and with the advancement of medical technology, all unreasonable criminal behavior can be prevented in advance.

Is Being Thin Better Than Being Fat? 222

— Xinong

People often say: "Although a person is thin, their bones and muscles are good." Science has proven that this sentence contains a great deal of truth. Previously, Hentig in his book "New Nutrition" had a statistic that among 100,000 people, the ratio of mortality rates for thin, fat, and neither thin nor fat people was: 100 to 158 to 154. Recently, Professor Ke Shi Katuo of the University of Berlin conducted a practical study on this issue of "being thin is better than being fat" using animals. He first fed dozens of white mice with a mixture of nutritious substances such as milk and white bread, and then separated the thin ones from the fat ones, subjecting each to attacks by toxic bacteria. As a result, the mortality rate of the fat ones was much higher than that of the thin ones. Similarly, alcohol poisoning also showed a similar pattern. Therefore, based on this, we can conclude that: being thin is better than being fat!

The Second Estimated Report of National Cotton Production in 1933 235

The China Cotton Industry Statistics Association announced the second estimate of national cotton production in 1933 as follows:

Cotton Field Area 39,684,369 Mu

Ginned Cotton Production 9,838,286 Dan

Abandoned Field Area 575,091 Mu

The above estimate is based on (1) reports from eleven provinces, including Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang, as well as Shanghai and Tianjin; (2) it is based on the cotton crop conditions before September 25; (3) the losses suffered by cotton crops in various provinces before September 25 have been included in the calculation; (4) cotton fields are measured in Chinese Mu, and cotton production is measured in Dan (100 catties per Dan).

First Estimate 39,157,446 10,754,451

Second Estimate 39,684,369 9,858,286

The national cotton production this year was generally good in the first estimate, and there were high expectations for a bumper harvest. However, several provinces suffered from severe drought. At that time, the estimated cotton production in eleven provinces was 10,734,451 dan, with an average of over 27 catties of ginned cotton per mu. If the drought-stricken areas had timely rain, the average yield per mu could have reached 30 catties. Unexpectedly, after the first estimate, the drought-stricken areas had little rain, and the development of cotton crops was affected. Although the weather was sunny in autumn, it was only able to barely break even. In addition, the flood in Shandong Province, the flooding in Cao District, the unresolved drought in central Henan, and the flooding of the Han River in Shaanxi also caused reduced production. Finally, Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces suffered from two wind and rain events in September, resulting in significant losses. Therefore, although Hubei and Hebei provinces increased slightly, the average situation has slightly deteriorated.

In summary, the total cotton field area in the eleven provinces this time is 39,684,369 mu, an increase of 526,923 mu compared to the first estimate. Because the first survey this year was earlier, the late-planted areas in June had not yet finished planting, so the cotton field area increased this time. If the number of abandoned fields is added, the cotton field area planted this year reaches 40,259,460 mu, the highest number in the last ten years. The total cotton production is 9,838,286 dan, a decrease of 896,165 dan compared to the first estimate this year. Compared with the actual harvest in 1932, it increased by 1,732,649 dan, which is still the highest production in the last ten years. The average yield per mu was 27.2 catties in the first estimate, but it has now dropped to 24.8 catties, a decrease of 2.4 catties. There will be a third estimate, which will be released on December 15.
