Free Talk

Going South 244

— Xu Maoyong

If my character were stronger, I could stay in Shanghai; although I have no martial arts, I would fight with my skull to resist the wolf's tooth club. If my character were weaker, I would jump into the sea on this moonlit night with the mournful sound of waves; I am not the only one who cannot live in this world.

Unfortunately, my character is between strong and weak. I cannot fight desperately, nor can I desperately commit suicide. So, I have to leave!

Where to go?

I cannot go deep into the mountains or dense forests; after all, associating with monsters is still a non-feasible idea. I want to live, and I still need to live among people. I want to leave the crowd in Shanghai and live in another crowd. In another crowd, the nets are not so dense, and the dead ends are not so many. I can still find a piece of land to manage my profession: start some fires and smelt some iron. Although crises are also lurking, they are not as urgent as in Shanghai. People with characters like ours can only survive like this. If even that place cannot survive, I may no longer love my life. However, now I am fleeing from Shanghai with my life.

Shanghai, you devil-infested Shanghai, I am leaving you.

"I am going south again. I laugh at how the phoenix and luan are tossed about this year, what is my mood like? Even if my writing amazes the world, it is just pale and weak on paper; what does the spring water have to do with me? The evening rain suddenly comes, and the wild geese disappear, amidst the vast mountains and autumn sounds, urging the guest to leave, leaving like water..."

These are Ding Ling's sentences again. Why do her words often move me? But how can I compare to her? How can a "fallen people" who do odd jobs in the cultural world have amazing writing? Although there are many authors in the current literary world who "become famous with a little emotion," how dare I hope for that! "Pale and weak on paper" is really irrelevant to society, but for myself, it will cause death. It is really not worth it to waste my energy and life like this. I'd better leave!

Goodbye, you devil-infested Shanghai. I am going to another crowd. But I do not have such a delusion: "I wish I could get three million gold coins, make friends with all the beautiful women and famous scholars, and make friends with all the chivalrous people of Yan and Han." I just want to go to the people who provide rice, wheat, cloth, and silk, to manage my profession; start some fires and smelt some iron.

Buddhist Socialism 245

— He Ru

Christian socialism has already been discussed, and I want to talk about Buddhist socialism. But I have no connection with Buddhist scriptures, and I cannot say any great Buddhist principles. I just happened to read the Yuan Dynasty Zaju Anonymous's "Coming Debt," so I will base it on this miscellaneous drama.

"Coming Debt" tells the story of Pang Yun of Xiangyang in the Tang Dynasty giving up his wealth to become a Buddhist. It tells the story of Li Xiaoxian borrowing two silver coins from Layman Pang for business, and he should return four silver coins with principal and interest. Unfortunately, he lost his money and had no money to repay. One day, he passed by the county government and saw more than a dozen people tied up and beaten in the yamen, all because they owed the rich man money. He was shocked and worried and became ill. Layman Pang learned of the cause of the illness, and because he had been helping people in need, he thought it was to do good deeds, but who would have thought that it would become an injustice? He burned Xiaoxian's IOU in front of him and gave him two silver coins. Layman Pang returned home and burned the documents of money lent to people in recent years. Unexpectedly, the smoke soared into the sky, alarming the God of Increase of Fortune in the upper realm, who transformed into a scholar and asked Layman Pang under the name of Zeng Xinshi. The two discussed the use of money, and the Layman thought that money was evil. They agreed to meet again later and parted. In the evening, the Layman burned incense in the front and back yards of his house. He saw the suffering of the mill doctor Luo He beating the gong and driving the cow. He asked him to stop working and gave him a silver coin to make a living. The mill doctor got the silver but could not sleep all night and returned the silver. The Layman also heard the voices of donkeys, horses, and cattle at the back trough when he burned incense in the evening. The donkey said, "Brother horse, why did you come here?" The horse said, "I owed Layman Pang fifteen taels of silver, and I had nothing to repay him. After I died, I became a horse to repay him. Brother donkey, why did you come here?" The donkey said, "I owed Layman Pang ten taels of silver, and I had no money to repay him. After I died, I became a donkey to grind the mill for him. Brother cow, why did you come here?" The cow said, "Don't you know? When I was alive, I borrowed ten taels of silver from Layman Pang, and the principal and interest were twenty taels. I never repaid him, so I am now a cow to repay him." Layman Pang was shocked when he heard this and said, "Hey! It scares me to death! I originally did good deeds, but who would have thought that I would turn out to be doing bad deeds! Isn't this all coming debt!" So he called his family and told them what he had heard from the cattle and horses. He burned all the documents of his family's wealth. He gave each of the servants in the family one tael and a deed of freedom and sent them home. He sent all the cattle, sheep, donkeys, mules, and horses to Lushan Mountain to be released. All the gold, silver, treasures, jade utensils, and trinkets were sunk into the East China Sea. The whole family went to Lushan Mountain to grind bamboo and weave sieves for a living. Finally, the whole family attained enlightenment and became Buddhas.

This play contains problems such as high interest loans, employee treatment, livestock treatment, the abolition of money, the liberation of slaves, and the sacredness of labor. The central idea is an attack on the private property system. But the author could not find a proper solution and concluded with the Buddhist theory of cause and effect and reincarnation, hoping that the exploiting class would lay down their butcher knives. This kind of fantastic Buddhist socialism is naturally ridiculous in the eyes of people with correct ideas in modern times. Moreover, the play assumes that the poor class, who are exploited by landlords and creditors and unable to bear it, will have to become cattle and horses after death to repay their debts, which is even more unforgivable nonsense.

Demon's Lair – Impressions of Qingdao, Part Three 246

— Ke Ling

On one side of Zhan Mountain, the woods shelter four enormous gun emplacements, lined up like stone turtles craning their necks, their mouths facing the sea bay where the water meets the sky, and the clouds and mountains are vast.

These gun emplacements were built when the German Empire occupied Jiaozhou. Qingdao passed from German hands to Japanese hands, and then was "received" back from the Japanese. After enduring vicissitudes, what remains is this painful historical relic.

Now the gun emplacements are useless, but you can still go inside. The entrance is on the mountainside, where there is a mottled iron gate, covered with moss and vines.

Inside, it's just like a terrifying demon's lair!

There is boundless darkness, and a pungent odor permeates the gloomy air. The ground underfoot is damp and slippery, and stepping on it will make the hairs on your body stand on end. A child who guards the gun emplacements leads the way, holding a lit candle, moving faintly along a narrow alley. What your eyes see is: a trembling candlelight, a circle of dim yellow light, the child's head within the light, dilapidated walls; besides these, there is nothing else. At this time, if you have any feelings, it must be the scenes of demon lairs described in fairy tales that come to mind.

But what is in front of you is not a mountain cave filled with jagged rocks, nor is there a residence for giants and elves – a magnificent and exquisite mysterious palace.

It is the modern architecture we often see, killing machines made of white stone and steel. There is a railroad track for transporting vehicles underground, leading directly outside; overhead there are steel rails for transporting artillery shells. Inside, in addition to the places where the gun positions are installed, there are many small rooms: this is where the generators are installed, that is where the artillerymen rest; this is the kitchen where food is cooked, and the rusted large iron pot is full of mud, said to be beef; that is the infirmary for wounded soldiers, and in the blurred light, the child who leads the way points to the spots on the wall: "These are bloodstains of wounded soldiers."

From these places, you can imagine how, years ago, those young German soldiers lurked in narrow cellars, moved the machinery of the cannons, and fired fiercely at the enemy, calmly and unhurriedly doing the work of killing.

But they were not evil demons either. They were young people deceived by the doctrine of iron and blood, they killed many brothers of different races like themselves, and as a result, they themselves became wandering souls in a foreign land. Perhaps those spots on the wall are their blood and tears of repentance.

The place is more than a mile long, and the other side is also a rusted iron gate. Only when you go out from there do you see the bright sunshine again. It is said that when this huge project was built, none of the Chinese residents of Qingdao knew about it; it was not until the German soldiers withdrew that these destroyed gun emplacements were discovered. Poor Chinese people, they are often killed in a dreamlike state.

Yuan Zhonglang as an Official (Continued) 247

— A Ying

He called himself a "messenger on the go" (like Guan Ning in his early days), and even said, "The suffering of holding documents is worse than being ill; the pleasure of clerical work is more hateful than medicine" (with Huangfu Erquan), and believed that "since taking the position of Magistrate of Wu, it has been like wearing a thousand layers of iron armor," and only "without officialdom is one's body light" (with Xi Weichang). Official life, in his conclusion, is simply "one day in office, one day in living hell" (with Luo Yin Nan), and being an official is like "a bitter ascetic monk" (with Wang Baigu) only! Therefore, "when the elders of the village presented a petition," he "would write on the back of the paper" (with Liu Zigan), saying:

Far from home, my heart is lazy, how can I be a wandering official;

Little food, many affairs, I fear I am a guest of eternal sleep!

You can imagine how much Zhonglang suffered from being an official. However, in fact, he had another layer of suffering, that is, he was originally a carefree, unrestrained person, and if you forced him to engage in such a busy and lowly life all day long, completely cutting him off from his past life, he could not help but feel uncomfortable. In his letter to "Lan Ze Yun Zeshu," he once mentioned this matter:

The capital city is prosperous, but being an official is suffering. Why? Boats, pens, drums, singing boys, and dancing girls are the affairs of generous guests, not the affairs of officials. Strange flowers, rare plants, dangerous rocks, and lonely peaks are the sights of reclusive men, not the sights of officials. Wine parties, poetry clubs, vermillion gates, purple lanes, shaking clothes on the peak of Mo Li, and washing feet on the stone of Tiger Hill, are the pleasures of tourists, not the pleasures of officials. What the officials face are the grain chiefs with patched clothes, the cunning people with glib tongues, and the prisoners covered in lice.

A carefree and unrestrained person cannot be a "generous guest," a "reclusive man," or a "tourist" because he is an official. How can he not be indignant and seek to leave? This is why Zhonglang said the following words in his letter to Tang Yireng:

How many days does life have? In long forests and abundant grasslands, what is not suitable? Yet one makes oneself suffer so. Every time I look at Tao Qian, it is not that he did not desire to be an official, nor that he did not hate poverty, but the desire to be an official could not overcome his love of ease, and the hatred of poverty could not overcome his厭厭of toil, so he finally returned, preferring to beg for food rather than regret it. Why did Zhonglang not want to be an official? This is also one of the reasons, "Officialdom is tiring, far不如carefree散散can suit one's ambitions" (with Tao Shikui). To understand Zhonglang's ambitions, you can see the whole picture in this letter. A life that is not suitable for him is forced upon him, how can he not "accumulate fatigue and become ill," and indignantly resign from office? In the past, when reading the family letters of Wu Linzheng, who died for the country at the end of the Ming Dynasty, there was a saying, "Although I have an honest heart, people will also forgive me, but every time I wake up in the middle of the night, I think I am not a person of the official path," like Zhonglang, judging from his temperament, he is not a "person of the official path"!

Goddess (Two) 248

— Shi Heng

In this way, we sat opposite each other across a square table, not saying anything, each of us thinking about different things in our hearts; she must be wondering about this ridiculous man, who used money to recruit a woman who would not refuse no matter what, but was so civil; at the same time, I was thinking, although it was the power of money that brought us together – she sacrificed her body for a night to get a few dollars, and I spent a few dollars to indulge my lust for a night, but for me, this matter did not seem so simple at all. "You called me here, why don't you say anything?" Finally, she could not bear it anymore and said something like this. "I don't speak your language!" I still replied to her happily like this.

I knew that this woman did not understand my words either, although when I asked her, "Do you understand my words?" she replied, "I understand, I can also speak Mandarin." But even her Mandarin, I still could not understand.

"Could it be that you don't 'fancy' me?" Although she said this with a smile, there was a pitiful look in her smile. "No, absolutely not!" In order to reassure her, I could not help but answer like this.

But then I did not know what to say, and the silence continued for a long time. She nervously touched the purse she had brought, looking around, looking at the wall, looking at the ceiling, she seemed unable to understand what she had come here to do.

I understood very well how much embarrassment she was enduring in her small heart, which was accustomed to enduring pain, because if you bluntly answered her "I don't fancy you," she would smile charmingly and pounce on you, trying to make you fancy her; but now, the dull air of this dirty little room, and that face that smiled at her but was actually devoid of warmth, made her not know how to deal with it, all her tricks were useless. This was simply a more severe insult than anything else for her.

Although I understood her state of mind very well, I could not think of anything to say, partly because of the language barrier, and partly because in this kind of environment, I really did not know what kind of words to say. After thinking hard for a long time, I finally said this:

"Why don't you go to bed and sleep for a while?" As I said this, I used gestures to help my words, so that she could understand what I meant. She smiled contemptuously, obviously she misunderstood what I meant, but I did not want to argue. Because in this kind of environment, I had already become her slave, and if I could reduce the unease in her heart, I would be infinitely comforted. So I still looked at her with a smiling face, watching her unbutton her buttons. Under her white silk cheongsam, there was a light red undershirt, and two small nipples were slightly protruding inside. The flames of lust that had been suppressed in my chest were burning again.

"Turn your face away, don't look!" She deliberately said these words shyly. But these words were full of temptation, and my heart was beating violently.

Unexpectedly, I really lowered my head, picked up a pen at hand, and scribbled on the paper. When she took off her clothes and wrapped her body in the quilt, I heard her shout "Silly boy!" as if she had discovered something.

On the Topic of Occupations Wen Bing

In the present situation where rural economies are withering and urban markets are experiencing recession, with a double dose of intensification, related professions have long since become an enormous problem. Countless people have circulated outside the circle of occupations for years, but still find themselves jobless and unable to be employed, forming a widespread unemployed panic amongst those who are adrift and hungry. So, what is there to say about occupations? However, in reality, there are indeed many people who have achieved success in finding employment, and this is certainly one of life’s greatest questions. Everyone should have some recognition and understanding of this, so it is worth discussing.

The definition of the two characters for “occupation” can be found in dictionaries as: “The undertaking which one ought to perform within one’s role,” a meaning that seems too vague. I remember hearing a lecture on occupations by Mr. Jiang Hengyuan once, and his explanation was roughly as follows: “Duty is responsibility, and the undertaking is business. To do business with a sense of responsibility is called an occupation, and its journey is to benefit both oneself and others, in order to fulfill humanity’s divine task.” This kind of explanation from the literal meaning still cannot satisfy us. From an economic perspective, the so-called occupation is originally no more than a behavior that occurs in a certain fixed way, in order to obtain the means of living. Saying it this way, a certain object is merely economic, and the meaning is inevitably too narrow. We believe that the explanation of an occupation should be a kind of inevitable and necessary life activity of humanity, the course of which is to solve the problem of living and promote human society.

Here it is necessary to briefly state the meaning of humanity: one is to live, and the other is how to be able to live. Because to live, one needs the provision of clothing, food, and shelter. Because one needs the provision of clothing, food, and shelter, one needs life activities, which is to say, one needs to seek what is needed for life from one’s own labor. Today, of course, there are many people who, by relying on the private ownership system and social forces, can live comfortably without working. But this is obviously a distortion of the meaning of humanity, a morbid social phenomenon, the collapse of which is bound to come in the near future. Therefore, in the final analysis, humanity should have life activities, which is to say, humanity should have an occupation.

Because an occupation is so important to the meaning of life, the mutual relationship is also the closest. We know that if it is an occupation, it must have permanence, and it is like a shadow that closely follows one’s life forward every day. Therefore, at the beginning of employment, it is necessary to think carefully and cautiously. First, one must consider one’s own interests. Second, one must see whether one’s talents and abilities are a good match. Third, one must see how one contributes to society in general. These are the three basic conditions. A person with a scientific mind whose interests are very close to industrial occupations, but who goes to serve as an editor for a literary magazine, the result is bound to be that he himself feels bored and nothing is achieved. A junior high school graduate is asked to be an elementary school principal, which is also beyond his abilities. If an organization that manufactures and sells red pills, opium, and gambling equipment has a job for you, even if it is a good position, you should not rashly take it, because it violates the third condition. Not only is there no general social contribution, but it is simply a den of sin that harms society and the human masses. It cannot be said to be an occupation.

Therefore, at the beginning of employment, it is necessary to be strictly cautious, and the occupation that is obtained in accordance with the conditions must be one where talent is suitable for the occupation, and the occupation is suitable for talent. Then one should "respect one's work," "enjoy one's work," and "persevere in one's work." In fact, if it can be so allocated, then everyone who is unemployed will have work, everyone who has work will enjoy it, and everyone will work hard for the individual and for society as a whole.

However, the current society is too contradictory. There are many people who have no means of living and have to beg for food, who often have nothing to do. At the same time, there are people who have money, who often eat without working. People who can work and are willing to work often have nothing to do for them. People who cannot work often occupy the positions of those who can work, taking large amounts of money and eating well. In the final analysis, it is extremely difficult to seek employment now. Besides having the qualities of flattery and boasting, and having the support of power,

Society is like this, I will not say more. What I hope is that friends who already have an occupation and those who are seeking an occupation with certainty should thoroughly recognize the essence and importance of an occupation, and not be careless or negligent.

To a Deceased Friend Bin Fu 249

My friend was an ordinary person, but "death" is an extraordinary thing -- at least we ordinary people think it is -- and an extraordinary thing has actually befallen my ordinary person. I can't help but feel something, I cried.

In this day and age, it is extremely common for extraordinary people to suffer extraordinary deaths. However, that an ordinary person like you should die so easily, I simply cannot believe it!

When I received the news of your death, the "death notice" really couldn't make me believe it. I presumptuously made a phone call to your father, whom I did not know, and learned that your father had just returned to Shanghai from Hankou and was about to return to his hometown to prepare your body, which proved that you had indeed been taken by the god of death. In this unfamiliar conversation between two people, your father cried sadly, cried so much that I couldn't hear what he was saying, so much that I couldn't listen anymore, and I hung up the phone.

You and I had six years of close friendship. Needless to say, your death is a deep pain to me, but my sorrow is really nothing compared to your father's wailing, your mother's heartbreak, your eighty-year-old grandmother's grief, and your newlywed wife's disheveled hair and clawing face! It's really nothing!

Like you, an honest person who never violated the world or offended anyone, I don't think you would have any resentment towards "death." As the Greek Lucian said: "... Hunger, thirst, and cold are no longer your lot! You are gone, beyond the power of disease, ... love can no longer disturb your peace, harm your health, or invade your purse, ... you will not go to that hateful old age again, nor will you be an eyesore to your descendants again! ..." Death may be a kind of love for you.

On the other hand, the grief of your grandmother, parents, and wife is the only thing you are uneasy about, but how can we stop their grief!

I cannot experience what good there is in life, I cannot imagine what defects there are in the "underworld," and after careful thought, I have no reason to be sad for your departure!

September 22nd, on an autumn night with lamp light and rainy evening.

For the Sake of Money Shi Ben 250

(A scene of social darkness!)

The world is declining day by day, and morality and shame are lost – there is actually such a brazen woman in broad daylight, in a bustling city, disregarding shame and boasting about her ugly history of carnal instincts. Perhaps in the bizarre and lascivious Shanghai metropolis of the human flesh market, this is a common and unremarkable scene! But when I, an old country bumpkin who is still connected to "moral concepts," heard it, I couldn't help but be astonished and horrified.

"Dead turtle! Roadside corpse! Have you forgotten? Three years ago, you came to Shanghai with nothing in your hands, who made you what you are today? If it wasn't for this old woman risking her life, losing her face, and letting people sleep with her snow-white body! How could you be where you are today. It's not that I'm shameless to say it. It's not that I crave pleasure, it's for the sake of money that I gritted my teeth and endured the pain, alas! I worked hard for three years, and finally earned some money, but now you're enjoying it, not only eating ready-made meals, but also going out to whore and gamble every day, and that whore is your confidante, and you take money so lightly! Humph! This money didn't come easily, it's this old woman's blood (of course not "tendon") and sweat, every coin has bloodstains on it! Can it withstand you dancing, watching operas, and keeping women like a young master's life of luxury? Wouldn't you squander the few stinking money I earned with my body? Dead turtle! To be honest with you, if you dare to continue wasting money like this, I'll cut you off completely! See what you'll rely on to live then?" On the bustling ×× Road, where cars and horses were shuttling back and forth, the boss lady of a single-fronted cigarette and paper store, roaring angrily, with her willow eyebrows standing on end, her almond eyes wide open, her face turning ashen, was pounding the table and bench in the store, flying into a rage, and scolding her trembling husband, who was standing in the corner of the counter, with his head hanging down.

The sound of scolding and cursing alarmed the people coming and going on the road, and in an instant, many people gathered on the sidewalk to watch the fun. At the same time, everyone was secretly whispering: "Look! How pitiful this man is! His face is pale and he is shrinking in the corner, timidly not saying a word in return, letting this she-tiger scold him endlessly without any restraint, it's a shame he's a man, he's so afraid of his wife!" A person in the crowd said indignantly.

"It's not that he's afraid of his wife, he's afraid of 'money'! Did you hear? He relies on his woman's ability to eat and drink, of course he should be subject to her control, how dare he resist her?" Another said this way. "Such loud吵吵吵吵吵吵ing, isn't it embarrassing for others to laugh at? Alas! Don't wash your dirty laundry in public!" A Taoist student said with a sigh. "There are countless tricks of 'women supporting men' on the Shanghai Bund! There are piles of fat cats who eat fine food and rely on women to make a living!" "Brother, you're right! Not to mention small people, relying on women's faces! Even some of the famous big shots now, many of them rely on the luck of their female relatives."

"Dead turtle! Roadside corpse ... this money is your woman's snow-white body ... pain ..." The boss lady was still scolding endlessly. He in the corner, after hearing so many people outside saying cold words and sarcastic remarks, and she was constantly exposing her own ugliness, suddenly became ashamed and angry, his face turning red and white, his eyebrows standing on end, his teeth clenching, thinking of hitting her, but then he suddenly remembered how poor he was when he came to Shanghai empty-handed three years ago! If it weren't for his wife's ability, and she had hooked up with Old Man Zhang, how could he be where he is today? This stinking skin would have been buried among the white poplars and barren grass long ago, and would he still have the good fortune to be a boss in a big city? Besides, his wife now has twenty or thirty thousand in hand, so for the sake of money, he had to endure it! Face doesn't matter, anyway, now it's "only serving the clothes, not the person." So his body softened again, and the hand he was preparing to hit her with involuntarily retracted, his face burning hot, his head dizzy, still not moving in the corner. "Woo woo woo" A bright and dazzling car arrived and stopped at the entrance of the ×× cigarette and paper store, the car door opened, and an elderly man with a mustache, wearing a gentleman's outfit, with a cigarette in his mouth, stepped in. The boss lady, who had a face full of anger and murderous intent, instantly became soft and smiling, greeting him happily and walking hand in hand with the old man. This ugly drama also came to a sudden end.

"Extremely Ordinary Things" Zhi 251

After teaching for two hours in night school, with today's salary of one dollar and forty cents just received in my pocket, I moved my tired body heavily to the bus stop on Nanjing Road with an unknown feeling of joy, sorrow, relief, or bitterness. It was at this stop that I encountered something that many people would say was an "extremely ordinary thing." -- Really, this thing is both "ordinary" and simple.

In front of the gate of a brightly lit ham store, a large crowd of people gathered. In the core of the crowd, I found four people who could draw my attention: one was a rickshaw puller who was still panting and whose short shirt was soaked with sweat, revealing his chest, and in his dark and rough palm he was holding "eight small coins" that looked strangely unsightly, and it seemed that his heart was filled with a belly of grievance and unsuppressible anger; two were dignified "gentlemen" in blue uniforms holding police batons; and one was a young shop assistant dressed neatly like a gentleman, who was gesticulating, but was speaking to our "gentlemen" with a kindly and softly manner, explaining his reasons. Our "gentlemen" crossed their arms in front of their chests, leisurely listening like a judge examining a prisoner.

"How far is it from here to Ferguson Road? We agreed on five dimes; because I couldn't find the destination, I asked him to pull me back. I added thirty cents, and he made me run in vain, so I paid him eighty cents in total. I ask you, gentlemen, did I owe him anything?"

"Is this your reasoning? No matter what, it's been almost three hours since I started pulling at six thirty, and I've run dozens of miles. I haven't even had dinner yet!" A trembling, but really angry, voice spewed out of the throat of this stubborn worker like rising smoke. Then, our "gentlemen" interrogated him coldly and briefly:

"So, how much do you think you should get?"

"In principle, I should get at least ten dimes."

"Add twenty cents."

A victorious smile floated on the face of the young shop assistant dressed like a gentleman. Obeying the "gentlemen's" judgment, he counted out twenty cents to the rickshaw puller; but the rickshaw puller was still arguing righteously and not agreeing. So

"Pig! You don't know what's good for you! I'm helping you, and you don't appreciate it at all? Get out!" The police baton was raining down on the frame of the car. So the rickshaw puller dragged the car away in a panic.

Next, there were these varied discussions from the onlookers:

"You don't need to talk nicely to this kind of guy: if you give him a little color, he'll want to open a dye house. A petty person is always a petty person!"

"The rule is three dimes an hour for a rickshaw."

"If you don't speak fiercely at the beginning, and ask for more money nicely and kindly, people will always be willing to add it."

"…………………"

Moving forward, I was squeezed into a corner. "Three dimes an hour," "If you want to add money, you have to speak nicely" I repeated to myself.

Longing After Farewell Due To 252

It was an afternoon in late autumn, at the foot of Zhao Bao Mountain, only some scattered rocks and withered grass remained. The faint setting sun was slanting upon the silent Zhongshan Mountain. Waves of geese were calling to each other, all flying down into the reed marshes. Flocks of crows were cawing noisily, flying south. There was a wisp of floating cloud in the sky, and the pure blue sky, apart from the flying and calling geese formations and crow flocks, was completely unadorned. The harsh wind was blowing against the withered grass on and around the mountain, seeming to play a kind of bleak music. I looked up and saw a ship with yellow smokestacks moving straight ahead, slowly about to sail out of the harbor. She—she is my mother!—how is she pondering her only beloved son on the ship? A week of time has passed so quickly. Now my mother has left me again, drifting far away on the boundless ocean. I am a helpless orphan; my father has returned to the yellow earth, sleeping peacefully on the top of Sand Crab Ridge. Even if I desperately and sorrowfully call out "Dad!", he would still ignore me. He and I are now separated by the realms of life and death, with no hope of reunion. Now my mother has also gone far away. The smoke from the smokestacks is drifting farther and farther, eventually disappearing and becoming invisible! Ah! How unbearable it is in my heart! My mother has been taken away by that merciless and cruel ship. This hateful, cursed ship, aren't you too cruel?

The words my mother嘱咐 told me before boarding the ship are now replaying clearly in my mind, and I feel that every word and every sentence contains great love. Such loving words, there is definitely no one else in the world who can say them! At that time, I felt that my life could not be separated from her love. So I wandered on the small path at the foot of the mountain, gazing at the dome-shaped azure sky and the vast sea. However, I felt apathetic to everything in nature. In my eyes, only my mother's image was very clearly reflected. Another flock of geese flew across the sky, with a burst of loud cries, which instantly broke the surrounding silence. On this bleak autumn evening, hearing a few loud cries in the long sky made me even more melancholic and hesitant. Looking at the surrounding gray-yellow, bleak, and deserted cliffs, I felt a deep, heavy, boundless, and indescribable sense of misery in my heart! The setting sun had completely sunk, and the remaining red light in the west was still shining obliquely on the earth. The mountain had changed from a floating purple to a deep gray. The harsh wind was blowing even harder, making me shiver involuntarily!

Class Notes by Yan 253

Ding! Ding! Ding! The school bell rang, and male and female students walked into the first classroom shoulder to shoulder.

Everyone walked into the classroom, and each student's gaze first focused on the few lines of chalk writing on the blackboard at the front, something about "New Mencius," something about "Western-style houses are what I desire, beautiful women are also what I desire. If I cannot have both, I will give up the Western-style house and choose the beautiful woman."

As everyone was laughing in bursts, I heard the sound of slippers walking behind me, seemingly approaching. Sure enough, Mr. Chen, who was nearly forty years old and had a haggard face, came in.

Mr. Chen walked onto the platform and began to say, "This class is about practical writing." After saying that, he took the chalk and copied the company organization law from the teaching book he brought, listing articles such as: one, name; two, purpose; and official document formats, such as requesting matters... earnestly requesting review and implementation, and other formats.

After copying a large paragraph, he took a cigarette from the cigarette case, lit it, and smoked it hard. Suddenly, the room was filled with smoke, and the students seemed to be lost in a fog, which made everyone laugh incessantly. However, Mr. Chen, pretending to be taking classes in a university, continued to smoke his cigarette as usual, while continuing to copy on the blackboard.

S and W, who were known for their humor in the whole school, took advantage of Mr. Chen's back being turned to the students while writing on the blackboard to dance in pairs in the back, also singing English songs in low voices. At this time, the students laughed even harder, covering their mouths.

Mr. Chen finished copying to a certain point and left without waiting for the end-of-class bell to ring.

Calligraphy and Paintings by Modern Celebrities 254

Mr. Xu Tie Feng's Calligraphy (Brief Biography)

Xu Tie Feng is a native of Dantu, Jiangsu Province. His calligraphy is exquisitely superb, covering all styles such as Yu Bei inscription, Yin Xu oracle bone script, bronze inscription, stone drum inscription, seal script, iron-wire Han clerical script, Northern Wei, Jin and Tang regular script, and running-cursive script. Recently, he has become tired of traveling in political circles and resides in Shanghai, practicing calligraphy. Nowadays, calligraphy masters in the country are gradually declining, but Mr. Xu is learned and versatile, encompassing all styles, no wonder the art world praises him and his threshold is worn through by visitors.

Jade scrolls and cinnabar writings are national treasures. Remnant stalks remain

at the Hui family for years. Tie Feng

War and Peace (Three) (Nine) (Four-Act Play) Ling He 255

Act Three: Praise of Peace

Confidential Secretary: Last night, Madam's mahjong playing was really good. She fully drew triples and quads.

Maid: You dead pig, why can't you hold onto even such a small thing?

Madam: Your mahjong playing wasn't bad either. Didn't you also draw two triples? How much did you win?

Orderly: It was because it was too small that it fell to the ground and disappeared.

Confidential Secretary: Not much, only a hundred and fifty-odd dollars. How much did Madam win?

Madam: I didn't win much, less than sixty dollars.

Maid: I don't care about those things. You pay me back.

Orderly: If I pay you back, even if I sell my bones, it wouldn't be worth that much money. How about I give you my life?

Maid: Who wants your dog bones? Your life isn't worth a penny.

Madam: Mr. He, there is a small matter I want to ask you to do. Can you do it?

Confidential Secretary: What is it? Madam, just tell me what to do, and I will do my best to do it?

Maid: I don't care, if you don't find it, I'll beat you to death.

Orderly: You want to hit me? Then I'll tell Madam that you stole her diamonds.

Madam: I heard just now that a representative is going to be sent to Miyun to negotiate a ceasefire, is that so?

Confidential Secretary: Oh! About that, I already spoke to the Minister and decided to send Madam's brother.

Madam: Oh? You've already said that? Thank you so much! Did he agree then?

Confidential Secretary: Of course he agreed. He agrees with almost everything I say.

Orderly: Stop nagging, I found it. Damn it, I searched for a long time, and it was hidden in this bush.

Madam: Thank you so much!

Maid: Give it to me quickly.

Orderly: No, first give me a kiss.

Maid: No, give it to me first, then kiss. (They kiss through the window. The orderly quickly exits, and the maid also disappears.)

Madam: My brother has told me several times to recommend him to the Minister, but I keep telling him to wait a while, wait a while, and wait for an opportunity. Today, there is such a good opportunity. If Mr. He hadn't mentioned it, he would have forgotten about it again.

Confidential Secretary: Hmph, the Minister is too busy with his affairs, and he often forgets such small matters.

Madam: What's busy or not, anyway, it's my business, so he doesn't take it to heart.

Orderly: (From outside) Secretary He! That group of wild dogs is here again. Should they be received?

Madam: Where did the wild dogs come from?

Confidential Secretary: Hahahaha, he's saying that the group of newspaper reporters is here again. The Minister often scolds them for being wild dogs. You should let them in. There's no way to get rid of these things.

Orderly: Yes! (Exits)

Madam: Wild dogs, that's an interesting new term. Since the wild dogs are here, I have to leave too.

Confidential Secretary: Haha, but these kinds of dogs don't necessarily bite people, Madam.

Madam: Hahaha, they don't bite people, they just love to eat beef. If you give them beef, they will wag their tails at you and not bark. (Goes upstairs.)

Confidential Secretary: Ah, Madam's mouth is really venomous!

Madam: Am I venomous? You're the one who's good at it. Give them a whip and then a piece of beef, that's real skill. (Disappears) (A group of reporters, about six or seven people, swarm up.)
